Current Commentary

Prospects for the Settlement of Xinjiang 20

— Ming

Since Foreign Minister Luo Wengan's visit to Xinjiang, the internal problems seem to have come to an end. Diplomacy is also gradually becoming more moderate. Although the problems have not been resolved, judging from the surface, it will not expand again for the time being. However, if we carefully examine its content, it is not as easy to resolve as the optimists say, nor is it as hopeless as the pessimists say. In the past, China's governance of the border areas was based on a laissez-faire policy, with no specific plan. The central government only used a policy of restraint, requiring obedience was sufficient. In the border areas, they thought that the emperor was far away and they could do whatever they wanted, almost like an independent local emperor. Tibet was like this, Mongolia was like this, and even Xinjiang, even after it was changed to a province, was still like this. After Yang Zengxin fell and Jin Shuren fled from the new province, the political weaknesses were fully exposed and changes occurred. The religious conflicts became more and more intense. The history of Sheng Shicai and Liu Wenlong in Xinjiang is not yet deep. They only rely on the support of the Han people and foreign troops (such as the old troops of the Soviet Ma) to support their current situation. It seems that it is not easy. As for how to implement political measures, how to build up the economy, and how to communicate religious barriers, I am afraid that there is no preparation at this time. Therefore, Ma Zhongying's troops in Xinjiang can still take this opportunity to continue to cause disturbances.

The central government has twice sent senior officials to Xinjiang to have a more in-depth understanding of the core of the internal disputes in Xinjiang and the crux of the diplomatic problems. Before the specific measures for Xinjiang are distributed, we may as well offer some humble suggestions for the study of the people and to promote the attention of the authorities. First, if the current Xinjiang authorities still implement the political measures of Chang Jin and others, it will still not be enough to satisfy the hopes of the new people. How can they resolve the current disputes? Moreover, the north of the Tianshan Mountains was originally the center of national defense, and it is also a barren area. If there are no reliable measures to renew the previous state of decline, I am afraid that the alienated people will find it difficult to unite. Therefore, future governance must have a certain direction, and gradually progress according to local needs. For example, the popularization of education is the most important thing in today's Xinjiang. However, most of the Hui people in Xinjiang are unwilling to go to school, and some even destroy schools. If these prejudices are not eliminated, they will eventually become an obstacle to politics, and religious barriers will be more difficult to remove. Second, Xinjiang has abundant natural products. One is that transportation is difficult and difficult to develop. The other is that the peasant economy has just undergone transformation, and suddenly encountered political changes. It is even more difficult to reform the entrenched habits. Therefore, when it comes to development today, the first is to support the development of the agricultural economy, the second is to modernize livestock farming, the third is to develop transportation, and the fourth is to develop mining. Otherwise, without economic support, all measures will be difficult to implement.

The improvement of agricultural management is not only a problem in Xinjiang today. All parts of the country are in urgent need of it. However, the soil quality in Xinjiang is not as fertile as that of the three northeastern provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, and the land is sparsely populated. Therefore, the management of intensive agriculture, which cannot be realized in the densely populated areas of the interior, is quite easy to implement in Xinjiang. As for livestock farming, whether it is cultivating livestock or shearing wool and making leather, the government must first carry out model management to allow the people to learn from it, and then engage in the wool weaving and leather making industries. Then the future of light industry will be very promising. Transportation problem.

Now the Western Air Route has been opened, and it seems very convenient to travel back and forth. However, this kind of convenience has great value in terms of politics and national defense, but the benefits to the general social economy are very small. After all, how many people can afford to take airplanes with Xinjiang's backward economic power? Heavy goods such as Hami melons, wool, and leather cannot be transported by airplanes. This is very obvious. Therefore, if we want to develop the new province, we must engage in the development of railways, so that we can shoulder heavy responsibilities and go far. Although the cost is high, the effect is very significant. The construction of automobile roads is more beneficial than airplanes, but it can only benefit military use. The benefits to the entire national economy are also small. Because our country cannot manufacture automobiles and does not produce gasoline. Moreover, automobiles cannot carry heavy loads. Our country produces coal and iron. Now we abandon our own coal and use foreign gasoline. It is also uneconomical for the development of the national economy. Therefore, the completion of the Longhai Railway, extending to Dihua, and then extending from Dihua to the north and south of Xinjiang, is the most urgent plan for Xinjiang's transportation policy. The most important mineral resources in Xinjiang are oil, followed by gold and jade. However, the exploitation of oil mines requires huge capital. If railway transportation is not fully utilized, it will be difficult to avoid empty talk if we want to exploit oil mines.

In short, to clean up the difficult situation in Xinjiang and develop its huge resources, we must first renew politics, eliminate the Han-Hui conflict, and resolve all internal contradictions. Then the vast land will not repeat the mistakes of the Northeast.

Page 7

Hirota Advocates Peace and Moderation in Relations with Russia; Cites the Treaty of Portsmouth; Demands the Withdrawal of Soviet Troops 21

(Tokyo) Regarding the official recognition of Soviet Russia by the United States, some believe that it is intended to contain Japan. The views of the Foreign Ministry on this matter are as follows: After the Five-Minister Conference, the Empire's policy toward Russia has been decided, focusing on peaceful international policies to ease relations between Japan and Russia. Foreign Minister Hirota believes that the urgent task of the policy toward Russia is to promote the negotiations on the Middle East Railway, which have been stalled. At the same time, in order to avoid the danger caused by the concentration of Japanese-Manchukuo troops on the border, it is necessary to withdraw troops from the Russian-Manchurian border and stop military operations with each other. The Foreign Minister also stated that Japan and Russia had agreed in Article 9, Section 3 of the Treaty of Portsmouth after the Russo-Japanese War, which stated that "no fortresses or other military works shall be placed within the territory of Sakhalin Island at the 50th parallel and nearby islands," and also agreed that "no military measures shall be taken that would hinder the free navigation of the Soya Strait and the Tartar Strait." The spirit of this treaty can also be applied to the Russian-Manchurian border to eliminate military operations. Foreign Minister Hirota met with the Soviet Russian ambassador on the 6th and gave the above important hints. However, it is extremely important to pay attention to how Soviet Russia will respond to this. (Dentsu dispatch on the 11th)

(Tokyo) Because the United States is about to recognize its government, Soviet Russia is taking advantage of its international situation to show a challenging attitude toward Japan, and is also concentrating a large army on the eastern border to demonstrate. Moreover, on the 8th of this month, it protested against the intrusion of Japanese aircraft into its territory to suppress bandits, which was rejected by Foreign Minister Hirota. After these incidents continued to occur, relations between Japan and Russia deteriorated further. The Japanese Foreign Ministry believes that the root cause of this is that the Soviet Union has concentrated an unnecessary large army on the Russian-Manchurian border. Therefore, Foreign Minister Hirota decided to demand from the Russian government within days that its border troops be withdrawn to a certain area. That is, the item in the Treaty of Portsmouth regarding the establishment of a demilitarized zone on the border, which has always regulated the relations between the two countries and is still strictly effective today. Therefore, no soldiers are stationed on the Japanese-Russian border (50 degrees north latitude) on Sakhalin Island, and only stone tablets indicating the boundary are present, which can fully ensure the safety of both sides. However, after Japan and Manchukuo signed a protocol, Japan assumed the heavy responsibility of maintaining the治安 of "Manchukuo." The Soviet Union secretly concentrated an unprecedented large army on the border of "Manchukuo" or the northwestern region of Korea, and built defensive works. This action by the Soviet Union violated the Treaty of Portsmouth. Japan therefore demanded the withdrawal of Russian troops. Foreign Minister Hirota also proposed this matter when he met with Russian Ambassador Yurenev on the 6th. However, the Soviet Union's arrogant attitude remained unchanged. Japan has been patient and self-respecting, waiting for it to wake up. However, Russia still disregards international faith and maintains its current attitude. It has therefore decided that it is necessary to take decisive measures and notify the Russian government. (Nippon Rengo dispatch on the 11th)

Soviet Russia Conducts Strict Inspections of Pedestrians on the Manchuli Border 22

Manchuli Soviet Russia is conducting inspections on people of all countries passing through the Russian-Manchukuo border. Recently, it has suddenly become more serious. The belongings of those passing through must of course be inspected, and even the body is inspected, which takes two or three hours. Manchukuo believes that this action is a major humanitarian issue. The Manchukuo passport verification office has listed the facts of the victims and submitted them to Soviet Russia to urge it to reflect on its actions. If it still does not cancel the inspection, then all Russians passing through Manchuli must also be subjected to the same severe inspection, etc. Manchukuo has lodged a protest. (Dentsu dispatch on the 11th)

Zhang Xueliang Visits the British Prime Minister; Only a Private Social Occasion 23

(London) Zhang Xueliang and his wife went to the British Prime Minister's villa for lunch with MacDonald today. MacDonald hosted them because his son was invited by Zhang when he went to Manchuria in 1928. Therefore, this was only a private social occasion. (Reuters dispatch on the 11th)

US-Russia Diplomatic Resumption Closer to Reality; White House Agreement Draft Negotiated; Seeking Moscow's Approval 24

Negotiations Progress Smoothly; No Obstacles Encountered

(Washington) According to official sources, the draft agreement for the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia has been negotiated, and its content has been telegraphed to Moscow for approval. Today, Litvinov went to the White House to pay a visit to the US President and discussed for an hour or so. Although it was not possible to issue a statement recognizing Soviet Russia as expected, according to official sources, no serious obstacles occurred, and Litvinov had a smile on his face and told reporters that a joint statement would be issued soon. Then the White House did issue a statement, but it was still as vague as it had been, only saying that the President had discussed with Litvinov, the Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner, the issues discussed by Litvinov and Secretary of State Hull a few days ago. Now Litvinov will continue to talk with Hull and the President through regular channels. It is heard that when Litvinov and the President began negotiations this afternoon, both sides had a draft agreement. It was later heard that Litvinov will stay at the White House at the end of the week, and will have another meeting with the President tonight. At this time, most US officials admit that the talks between the two sides are progressing smoothly, and all major issues have been resolved. (Komin News Agency dispatch on the 10th)

Luo and Li Discuss Outstanding Issues 25

(Washington) After President Roosevelt and Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov met today, they issued a statement saying that they had discussed outstanding issues between the two countries, and that the talks between the two sides would continue to proceed along their usual path. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt and Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner Litvinov met again in the evening. The two sides have reached an understanding. According to political sources, as a result of the negotiations, the United States will soon recognize Soviet Russia de jure. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt is scheduled to meet with Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner Litvinov again at 7:00 pm on the 10th to discuss the issue of US recognition of Soviet Russia. According to White House sources, after tonight's meeting, there will probably be other meetings, and government officials will participate. The issue of recognizing Soviet Russia will not encounter any obstacles. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

(Washington) US President Roosevelt and Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner Litvinov discussed the issue of resuming diplomatic relations last night at 9:00 pm. The decision had not been made by midnight, and it is likely that there will be another meeting soon. A joint statement was issued this morning, but it is expected that the next meeting will be on Sunday afternoon, because the White House said that no talks will be held on Saturday. Litvinov told reporters that he and the US President had a most pleasant conversation, but there were no results to be announced. US Assistant Secretary of State Bullitt also went to the White House during the talks, but he did not make any statement afterwards. According to those who claim to be close to the President and Litvinov, the negotiations are progressing smoothly, but it is still necessary to meet again to eliminate some points of contention. It has not been stated which issues have not been resolved, but according to all unofficial sources, they are not serious. The outside world was disappointed that the resumption of diplomatic relations could not be agreed upon at this afternoon's meeting, because this matter has become an important factor for the market and trade, and cotton merchants are especially eager to recognize Soviet Russia as soon as possible. (Komin News Agency dispatch on the 11th)

Hull to Go to Uruguay; to Attend the Pan-American Conference 26

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull is scheduled to board a ship tomorrow to go to the capital of Uruguay to attend the Pan-American Conference. He has no plans to meet with Litvinov again before his departure. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

Tokyo Watching Development 27

(Tokyo) The US President's liquidation of the 16-year diplomatic rupture between the US and Russia, and the recognition of the Soviet Russian Federation, is almost certain. The Japanese Foreign Ministry observes its impact on the international community as follows: From a political point of view, the US's intention to recognize Soviet Russia is to attempt to equalize the power of European and American countries in the Far East. However, it is doubtful whether the US can realize this attempt. It is widely rumored that the US and Russia are cooperating to contain Japan, but this atmosphere is actually released by the Soviet Russian side. In reality, the resumption of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia has no substantial effect, but the extent of the agreement between the US and Russia and its impact are different. The most important thing to pay attention to is how many numbers the US will allow for Russian loans and the number of years of credit. This issue will begin to be discussed after the US recognizes Soviet Russia and exchanges ambassadors. (Nippon Rengo dispatch on the 11th)

Germany Has a Tendency to Return to Disarmament; Will Propose Reorganization of the League of Nations After the General Election; Italy Has Long Understood; France's Refusal Is Problematic 28

(Paris) According to reliable information obtained by the French government, it has been confirmed that after Sunday's general election, Germany will propose to reorganize the Council of the League of Nations and amend the organization and regulations of the League of Nations as a basis for Germany's re-entry into the League of Nations. According to reliable information obtained by Reuters, although Italy may agree to this proposal, the French government will refuse to accept it. According to sources in Geneva, after Mussolini's talks with Goering, Germany will seek Italy's consent in advance to propose that countries related to the German issue, such as Britain, France, Italy, Germany, Poland, Belgium, and the Little Entente, hold a meeting in Switzerland before the end of this year, but not in Geneva. France may accept this kind of meeting, but on the condition that the resolutions of the meeting are subject to the decision of the League of Nations. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

Rome According to a semi-official statement issued here today, the responsible authorities in Italy believe that the time to re-discuss the issue of disarmament and withdrawal from the League of Nations has not yet come. In the letter from Hitler to Mussolini recently handed over by General Goering, there were no concrete proposals for the Disarmament Conference. The letter only explained the progress of the Disarmament Conference and explained Germany's reasons for withdrawing from the League of Nations. General Goering explained several points in Hitler's letter, but he himself did not make any suggestions or ask the Italian government to propose any events. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

Rome The Italian Daily newspaper commented on the issue of disarmament, saying that since there is no possibility of Germany immediately returning to Geneva, a new diplomatic negotiation method should be sought for the issue of disarmament. The recent meeting between German Prussian Prime Minister Goering and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is the first action of an international nature after Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference, which shows that there is still a possibility for countries to re-establish contact with each other. The newspaper concluded that although the environment is not safe, it is hoped that it will improve soon. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

Geneva Continues to Work as Usual; the Six-Person Committee Meets; Distributes and Studies the British Plan 29

(Geneva) Since Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference, some governments have advocated that the Disarmament Conference should continue to work and the Disarmament Convention should be established. However, the Italian government expressed opposition. The method decided by the six-person committee of the Presidium of the Disarmament Conference today proves that the countries advocating continued work have won. When the six-person committee of the Presidium met, the British representative always acted in concert with the French representative, and the representatives of the small countries also enthusiastically supported France. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

(Geneva) The six-person committee of the Presidium of the Disarmament Conference met today and decided to submit the method of distributing and studying the British disarmament plan to the plenary session of the Presidium tomorrow for approval, and suggested the establishment of two committees. One is to study the issue of military quotas and the reform of the military systems of European countries, and the Soviet Russian representative is specially invited to participate. The other is to discuss the issue of arms and sanctions, and the Soviet Russian and Japanese representatives will be invited to participate. If the Presidium approves this proposal, six people will be appointed as rapporteurs to sort out the following issues: (1) Security issues, to be handled by Polis, the Greek Minister to France; (2) Czech Foreign Minister Benes to handle the issue of arms and the opening date of the Disarmament Conference; (3) Polish representative Komarnicki to handle the issue of arms and ammunition manufacturing; (4) British representative Cadogan (the new Minister to China) to handle the issue of the publication of military budgets; (5) Dutch representative Moraes-Goes to handle the naval issue; (6) Norwegian representative Lange to handle the aviation issue. (Havas dispatch on the 10th)

Belgian MP Publishes Secret Documents Exposing German Unresolved Armament; Modified Several Times to Soften the Tone; Will Not Cause Serious Disputes 30

Brussels Belgian Foreign Minister Hymans wanted to prevent Senator Toutoulou from publishing the secret report of the Allied Military Committee but failed. Some evening newspapers have already published summaries, but they are not causing the outside world to be as shocked as some had predicted. According to the summaries published, if they are true, they only want to show that Germany has not fully fulfilled the obligations of disarming within the treaty, and do not mention the quantity. Toutoulou also said that this report had been greatly modified by the Ambassadors' Conference to soften its tone before it was sent to the League of Nations, in order to prevent serious disputes from occurring. However, he had obtained a copy of the original report. As for his intention this time, he only wanted to express that Germany had not disarmed, and did not provide concrete evidence of Germany's breach of contract. The general impression here is that this action will not cause serious impact, because it had already been said that Germany had not completely disarmed, and at this time, the powers are trying to persuade Germany to return to the Disarmament Conference. Toutoulou's actions are also inconsistent with the policy of the powers, and their effectiveness is naturally minimal. (Komin News Agency dispatch on the 10th)

Beijing Belgian Senator Toutoulou declared to the press today that Germany has absolutely not reduced its armaments in accordance with the Treaty of Versailles. Toutoulou's statement is based on the last unpublished report of the Allied Military Administration Committee, which was secretly printed in Paris in 1927. This report is only held by each Allied government, and has 514 pages. It states the difficulties of the committee in managing Germany's armaments, and lists Germany's cunning methods of retaining its armaments and secretly manufacturing prohibited weapons in chemical factories, and claims that Germany did not comply with Article 5 of the Treaty of Versailles in 1927. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

Hitler Expresses Willingness to Participate in International Negotiations on Equal Terms: The German People Desire Only Peace, Treaty Restrictions Hinder Survival 31

(Berlin) Today, Chancellor Hitler, in his final campaign radio address on Siemens Radio, stated that Germany is still willing to befriend its former enemies, and that Germany's security is no more threatened than that of other countries. Why is it that other countries do not trust Germany? Has East Germany ever broken its word? We are prepared to participate in any international conference, participate in any negotiations, and sign any treaty, but only on the condition of equality. I will never allow Germany to be relegated to a second-class status. If other countries do not want to grant us equal status, then we should not associate with each other, etc. (Reuter, 10th)

(Berlin) At 1:00 PM today, Chancellor Hitler delivered his final speech at the Siemens factory. The first part was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The following is the supplementary report of the second part: Hitler said that the current difficulties and hardships of Germany are entirely due to the Treaty of Versailles, and that the world economic panic is also due to various errors in international policy. The so-called international solidarity is just a theory. We must unite the various forces of the German nation to create a new German community. The nation cannot destroy itself through internal strife. We first unite all the German people to overcome general difficulties. The National Socialist Party is based on farmers and workers. The intellectual class has no courage to create such a community. Hitler then described the German government's recent war debts, and said that since he came to power, he has only had one intention, which is to heal the wounds that the Marxist policies have inflicted on Germany for the past fourteen years. We will try to remedy it and give credit and livelihood to the people. The new government will never exploit one class to benefit another. What it seeks is the welfare of all the German people. Hitler said that he deeply regretted that he could not clear up the damage caused by the improper actions of previous governments in one fell swoop. He then spoke of his four-year plan and foreign policy, saying that he had personally fought in the war and experienced its cruelty firsthand, which is contrary to the situation of some politicians. The German people only hope to work wholeheartedly in peace and are willing to join hands with enemy countries. The painful era of world history should now be brought to an end. Germany does not want to separate from other nations. All it seeks is to obtain equality of rights, because inequality is the most unbearable thing. So-called honor is the ability to enjoy equal rights. Germany does not want to be bound by treaties that are forcibly recognized. People often say that Germany cannot be trusted, but when has Germany ever broken its word? During the European War, if Germany had not been overly loyal to its allies, Germany would not have suffered such a bad fate. Germany is prepared to participate in all international work, but only on the condition of standing on an equal footing. Foreigners can always find sympathizers among the German nation, but "international vagrants" are not tolerated by Germany. After the election on November 12, foreign people should know that in the minds of the German people, there is only peace, honor, and equality of rights, because the survival of the German nation is something we must take into account, etc. (Havas)

Hindenburg's Speech on the Eve of the German General Election: Urges People to Support the Government to Fight for International Equality of Rights 32

(Berlin) President Hindenburg today sat next to a radio transmitter in the library of his private residence and delivered a moving speech to millions of listeners, asking them to support the government in the general election tomorrow in order to fight for equal rights and true lasting peace. Hindenburg praised Hitler's courageous and vigorous active policies, and said that the principles that Germany wants to strive for in its national life are work and construction internally, and peace, honor, and equality externally. No one in Germany wants war. The German government is very willing to jointly and completely disarm with all countries. Germany withdrew from the Disarmament Conference and the League of Nations because it did not agree with the idea of applying different means to victorious and defeated countries. The people of the country should proclaim to the world the fact that Germany has been unified, etc. (Reuter, 11th)

Austria Declares Martial Law: Destruction of Order Punishable by Death; Border Traffic Along the German Border is Blockaded 33

Vienna. The Austrian State Council today announced martial law. A government communiqué stated that serious cases of arson and destruction of order may be punishable by death by military tribunals. It also stated that this martial law is different from general martial law, but because the anniversary of the founding of the Republic of Austria and the German general election both fall on November 12, the Austrian government feels it is necessary to increase its strength to cope with possible events. (Reuter, 10th)

Vienna. Tomorrow (November 12) is the day of the German House of Representatives election. All demonstrations are prohibited throughout the province of Vorarlberg. The border between Austria, Germany, and Bavaria has been blockaded by the Austrian authorities since noon today. Only German citizens who have election tickets are allowed to pass through the border. (Havas, 11th)

(Tokyo) The two major radio stations in Tokyo and Berlin will exchange broadcasts at 4:30 PM on November 15 (Tokyo time), for a duration of twenty minutes, sending each other's ambassador's speech and the national anthems of both countries. The Tokyo radio station will also broadcast recordings of speeches by President Hindenburg and Chancellor Hitler. (Reuter, 11th)

German Social Democrats Denounce the Domestic Election as a Fraud 35

Prague. The headquarters of the German Social Democratic Party here issued a declaration denouncing the German election on Sunday, while discussing the unfortunate consequences of the National Socialist Party's policies at home and abroad. The declaration stated that the election was "a shameful fraud" and that some Germans, even under great threat, were still prepared to vote against Hitler and Goering's "bloody dictatorship" in Sunday's election. (Paris) Today, France held the 15th anniversary of the Armistice throughout the country. The ceremony was the same as in previous years. All public buildings, the presidential palace, the Senate and the House of Representatives, and various ministries in Paris were decorated with flags and colorful banners. The weather was gloomy and cloudy. From 8:30 AM, various delegations of disabled veterans of the war gathered in front of the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier. At 11:00 AM, the Paris garrison lined up to arrive at the scene, and the crowd surged. The Tomb of the Unknown Soldier under the Arc de Triomphe was filled with flowers. In the procession, there were military flags used by the 250th Regiment that had been retired, arranged in formation, led by a band, and General Gouraud led the way. The crowd took off their hats and saluted. Government ministers arrived at the scene first, followed by President Lebrun, protected by a cavalry guard. At exactly 11:00 AM, the artillery fired a cannon as a signal, and everyone was silent for one minute. Then, the Paris garrison began to parade in formation. At 3:30 PM in the afternoon, the unveiling ceremony of the memorial monument of former Foreign Minister Briand was held, presided over by Prime Minister Sarraut and many cabinet members. The Soviet Delegation Leaves Turkey for Home: Friendship Between the Two Countries Takes a Further Step 37

Istanbul. The Soviet delegation led by Voroshilov left Istanbul for Odessa today. When the Turkish authorities saw them off, they showed friendship and continued the warm and friendly attitude that Turkish officials and people had shown to the delegation during their stay in Turkey. Representatives of the Turkish government accompanied the delegation to Odessa. The Soviet delegation's stay in Turkey was an important stage in the development of Soviet-Turkish relations. The delegation held responsible talks with Turkish leaders, which confirmed that the views of the two countries on the struggle for peace were completely consistent. Before leaving, Voroshilov made a statement to Turkish and foreign reporters, saying that this trip gave the delegates a clear understanding of Turkey, its people, and its leaders. Voroshilov added, "The Soviet delegation observed with particular deep concern the achievements of Turkey in the construction of schools, youth education, women's liberation, industrial development, and railway construction. The current economic progress shows that Turkey can also be economically independent." Voroshilov also expressed his firm belief that the cordial reception of the delegation by the Turkish people, as well as the close and friendly contacts greatly strengthened by this trip, would enable the people of both countries to strive for peace with greater strength. The cooperation between the Soviet Union and Turkey is not only of special value to the people of both countries, but also to all friends of peace. Turkish Prime Minister İsmet Pasha issued a statement one day before the delegation's departure, saying, "Our talks with the delegation have joyfully shown that Soviet-Turkish friendship is more reliable than before. When the Soviet delegation leaves Turkish territory, it is necessary to once again represent the Turkish government and express to the government of the friendly country our most friendly confidence. The memory of the delegation's stay in our country will be unforgettable for us." (TASS, 9th)

Order Restored in Cuba: Rebels Surrender After Two Days of Bloody Fighting; An American Warship Sails to Protect Overseas Chinese 38

Havana. Although Cuba has experienced two days of bloody fighting unprecedented in its history, public order has now been fully restored. The rebels have all surrendered after being defeated by the National Army led by Colonel Batista. There are now a thousand rebels imprisoned in the fortress, awaiting trial by military tribunals. (Reuter, 10th)

Havana. The Cuban San Martin government today admitted that the situation here is still serious, and civilians should stay indoors. At the same time, an American training ship is said to have sailed from Danba to the Cuban capital. However, the dispatch of warships by the United States is not the result of discussions on intervention in Washington, but is merely an action to protect overseas Chinese. Cuban President San Martin changed his mind and declared the country in a state of war yesterday, and today declared Havana in a state of siege, asking the people not to interfere rashly and to wait for the federal government army to use force to resolve the rebellion. The number of deaths and injuries is increasing daily. Today it was reported that 200 bodies had been found in the rubble from yesterday's battle at Fort Atair in the suburbs. Today, the government issued a proclamation with strict content, ordering the army to use all weapons to punish the rebellion, because in the past, the government army had not let go because it was afraid of accidentally hurting civilians. Therefore, after the issuance of this proclamation, the whole city suddenly felt panicked, and the people immediately obeyed the order to stay at home and throw themselves out. Military officers also dispatched troops to distribute throughout the city. As for the situation in the outer provinces, although the government claimed that the government army had been able to quickly restore order, private news has not yet been verified. US Monetary Policy: Expected to Further Stipulate Silver Prices; US Dollar Has Fallen to Pre-War Levels 41

(New York) The US authorities today stipulated that the purchase price of domestically mined new gold is lower than the world gold price, so it can break the downward trend of the US dollar and limit its fluctuations to a very small range. The London foreign exchange market opened at a pre-war level of one pound sterling equal to five dollars and sixteen cents, but soon returned to five dollars and twelve cents. The decline in US bonds during the decline of the US dollar was caused by the Federal Reserve buying bonds in the open market every week, limited to ten million yuan. It is found that the Reserve Board used to take in bonds from 35 million yuan to 40 million yuan per week. (Nanjing) The Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Sino-British Joint Rail Contract expired in 1918. Due to the situation at the time, it was not possible to negotiate and revise it. In 1929, when Sun Ke was the Minister of Railways, he sent Xie Baoqiao to Bazhou to discuss with the British side, but the British side delayed on the pretext and did not achieve satisfactory results. Now it is heard that the railway authorities believe that this case has been delayed for a long time and needs to be revised urgently. They have ordered the relevant department to investigate the case and formulate a plan, and have ordered the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Bureau to sign an opinion and submit it to the ministry for reference. The Lanzhou-Qinghai Air Route Will be Slowly Established 46

(Nanjing) The Eurasia Aviation Company will not temporarily operate the Lanzhou-Qinghai air route. Zhu Jiaqi sent a telegram to Chairman Jiang, saying that the matter of the Eurasia Aviation Company's trial flight to Xining has been reported by telegram, and a reply has been received. According to Li Jingcong, the general manager of the company, he was ordered by telegram to send a plane for a trial flight to Qinghai. On September 24, Li Jingcong took the opportunity to inspect the Northwest route and flew to Xishou from Lanzhou with Eurasia Plane No. 2, along the Yellow River and the Xishui River. The voyage took a total of one hour, and the weather along the way was not an obstacle. The Xining Airport is also said to be suitable. Regarding the plan to open air routes to Qinghai and Xining, he consulted with Chairman Ma Lin and Division Commander Ma Bufang of the Qinghai Provincial Government, who said that the automobile transportation between Lanzhou and Xining can now be reached in only one day. Sometimes, due to muddy roads, there are delays, but at most it will not exceed two days. Even ordinary mail between Lanzhou and Xining can be received in only three boats and six hours. As for passengers and goods between the inland, there has never been much, so the shipping of mail by air, which consumes a lot of resources, is not urgently needed, etc. Li Jingcong completed the contact and set off to fly back. It is found that the transportation between Lanzhou and Qinghai is very convenient, and the commerce between the two places is not very prosperous. It is not necessary to urgently establish this route, which will increase losses. Therefore, it is approved to postpone the establishment and telegrammed Chairman Ma of Qinghai. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Issue of Passport Verification for Foreign Passengers on Eurasia Aircraft 47

(Nanjing) The Eurasia Aviation Company submitted to the Ministry, stating that the company's routes penetrate deep into the Northwest hinterland, especially since the opening of air routes to Dihua, the number of foreign passengers transported has been considerable. The company's sole purpose is to operate its business. Regarding foreign passengers going to the mainland, whether they should have passports or not, there has been a clear order, so it is inconvenient to overstep their authority and inquire. However, Xinjiang Province is located on the border and the situation is complex. In addition, it has recently been rumored that Britain, Russia, and Japan are all competing to instigate unrest in the province, causing the Chinese people to be motivated by patriotism and to be suspicious of the company every time it carries foreign passengers. For example, on the 6th of this month, a Shanghai newspaper widely published a Beijing dispatch stating that the company's plane carried Japanese military officers without passports to Lanzhou and Xinjiang, and the Xinjiang authorities telegraphed a request for their detention. The headline read in large characters, "Xinjiang Province Requests Detention of Eurasia Aircraft," implying that the company was negligent in paying attention to the foreign passengers' possession of passports, which was a mistake. Although this public opinion is inaccurate and speculative, it will inevitably affect the company's business prospects. In the future, whether foreign passengers going to the mainland should have their passports checked by the local authorities, or whether the company should also pay attention to whether they have passports, and whether all passports should be issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to be valid, so as to prevent risks and avoid blame, etc. The Ministry, believing that the matter concerns national defense and diplomacy, has consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for verification and reply, so that it can be instructed to comply. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

The Preparatory Committee for the Construction of the Qiantang River Bridge Has Been Established 50

(Nanjing) The Zhejiang Provincial Government plans to build a large iron bridge across the Qiantang River, and the Construction Department, led by Zeng Yangfu, has reached an agreement with the Ministry of Railways on cooperation methods. The Preparatory Committee for the Construction of the Qiantang River Iron Bridge has been established to carry out preparations. The required funds are planned to be borrowed from the Boxer Indemnity. The Qiantang River surface is about 400 meters wide, and a large iron bridge will be built. The planning drawings have been drafted. The iron bridge is annular in shape and does not hinder ship traffic. The bridge surface is divided into three roads: railway, motor road, and pedestrian road. The budget is 6.2 million yuan, and it is planned to borrow the British Boxer Indemnity. Zeng Yangfu once consulted with the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Association. The Ministry of Railways will formally send a letter to the Boxer Indemnity Association within a few days to borrow the funds. Reorganization of the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau by the Provincial Assembly 80

(Zhenjiang) Since Zeng Ji succeeded [to the position], the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau, the provincial government has decided to reorganize it, establishing one secretary, three adjutants, and two section chiefs (concurrently held by technical experts), and set four principles: (1) Implementation will be carried out based on available funds and personnel; (2) Measurement areas will be established in the provincial bureau, using counties as units. After the measurement and registration are completed, they will be handed over to the county governments to establish sections for handling, and then to other counties; (3) Counties without measurement sections will not establish bureaus, and sections that have already been established will be abolished; (4) Land surveying fees for each county will be handled in accordance with unified financial administration methods. The Heroic Martyrdom of Li Chunrun, Commander of the Liaoning Self-Defense Army, Repelled the Enemy's Fierce Onslaughts for Over a Year, Succumbing to Injuries Sustained in the Battle of Tagou 82

News from Peiping: Li Chunrun, Deputy Commander and Commander of the Sixth Route Army of the Liaoning People's Self-Defense Army, courtesy name Binpu, was 33 years old and a native of Fengcheng County, Liaoning. He was a graduate of the Beijing Army University, and was a patriotic and loyal man by nature. He served as an officer at various levels in the Northeast Army and participated in the anti-Russian war in 1929. After the September 18th Incident, Li was in Shenyang on official business and witnessed the true situation, becoming extremely indignant. He then fled back to the Eastern Border Defense Commissioner's Office in disguise and presented a plan for resistance against Japan to the Defense Commissioner Yu Zhishan. Because Yu had many concerns and did not adopt the plan, Li formed an alliance with comrades and waited for an opportunity. Soon after, he was transferred to serve as the commander of the Third Battalion of the First Regiment of the Liaoning Army Infantry, where he was able to carry out anti-Japanese work. On April 29, 1932, he joined forces with Tang Juwu to launch an uprising in Xinbin County and was appointed as the commander of the Sixth Route Army of the Liaoning People's Self-Defense Army. He subsequently participated in battles in Xinbin, Qingyuan, Fushun, Benxi, Fengcheng, and Kuandian, leading his troops bravely and striking terror into the enemy's hearts. When Tang Juwu failed last winter, Li retreated to southern Liaoning. Together with Deng Tiemei, Liu Jingwen, and his younger brother Chunguang (Zirong), and other commanders, he attacked the puppet army of Li Shoushan at Dagushan. Feeling a shortage of artillery fire, he came to Peiping in December to request assistance. He originally intended to return to his defense post as soon as possible to continue the fight, but on his way through the Yellow Sea, he and his family of seven were almost harmed by the Japanese, drifting on the ocean for more than a month. After receiving a large number of weapons and ammunition from various national salvation organizations, the coast was already frozen, making transportation difficult. In January 1933, he was appointed by the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association as the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Third Army Corps of the Northeast Volunteer Army. He immediately sent a number of cadres and comrades back to the Northeast to prepare for an uprising. Unfortunately, in Benxi, Dalian, and other places, 20 people, including Brigade Commander Sun Yaozu, were arrested and killed one after another. Li was filled with anger and vowed to redouble his efforts. In June, he was reassigned as the Commander of the Tenth Military District. In July, he returned to his defense area in Fengcheng County in disguise. Subsequently, commanders of various routes organized the National Volunteer Army and elected Li as the Commander-in-Chief of Liaodong, actively implementing political work and reorganizing the volunteer army. In that month, when the weapons and ammunition were transported there, it attracted the attention of the Japanese and puppet authorities. The Japanese sent Commander Ban Jin of the Japanese garrison to launch a fierce suppression against Li. Li was determined and unyielding, vowing to resist to the death. From the end of July onward, he repeatedly fought fierce battles with the Japanese army, with the Red Flag Street battle on the 30th, the Xie Jialing battle on August 2nd, and the Tagou battle on the 17th being the most intense. More than one hundred Japanese officers and soldiers, including Major General Commander Xiao Bin, were killed. The Japanese side considered it an unprecedented and miserable defeat against the Liaodong Volunteer Army, so they changed to an encirclement tactic to suppress the Volunteer Army. Therefore, Li's unit also changed its deployment, ordering Deng to lead all of the Sixth and Seventh Infantry Regiments to Sitai, Fenghuangcheng, Gaolimen, and Tang Li Chunrun's posthumous portrait

Shancheng, and other places to carry out sabotage work, and assigned the squadron leader to clear out the Japanese and puppet garrison troops in the Shalisai Shaozihe area, hoping to contain the communist forces. The enemy also mobilized elite troops to firmly defend the southern Manchuria and Anfeng lines, with a force of more than a thousand men, divided into three columns, attacking the general reserve force of the Volunteer Army. At 8:00 AM on August 17th, 300 Japanese soldiers were discovered at Shajinchang. The General Reserve Force of the Volunteer Army, two companies of Ao's division, totaling about 100 men, and the headquarters guard company of over 200 men, immediately launched a counterattack after the special task force detected the enemy's situation. At about 10:00 AM, they engaged the Japanese army at Tagou for about two hours. The enemy sent three bombers and three fighter planes from Andong to bomb the main force of the Volunteer Army and used machine guns for continuous strafing. At the same time, more than 200 Japanese soldiers arrived from the Dabujiapu area. After fierce resistance by the Volunteer Army, at about 3:00 PM, Li personally led the guard company to attack the left flank of the enemy. The fighting was extremely fierce. Li led his troops to charge forward and was shot in the upper part of his left thigh. He was then wounded by a hand grenade thrown by a Japanese soldier. The wound was about three inches deep, with bone fractures and flesh flying, and blood flowing non-stop. Li Chunguang directed the troops to fight on one hand and sent people to rescue him down the mountain on the other hand, and sent him to a secret place for treatment. In this battle, the Volunteer Army suffered losses that broke the record of previous battles against the war. Battalion Commander Zheng Anjun, two adjutants, three company commanders, and eight soldiers were killed in action. Over ten officers and soldiers were wounded. Major General Commander Xiao Bin, Lieutenant Colonel Ito, Captains Nakamura and Ihara, and 57 soldiers were killed. The number of wounded on the Japanese side is unknown. The Japanese also considered it an unprecedented and miserable defeat in Liaoning after the September 18th Incident and built a monument to the loyal souls in Tagou to commemorate it. Li was treated in the sixth district of Fengcheng. However, he was frequently searched by the Japanese and puppet troops, causing him great anxiety and preventing him from recovering. He secretly ordered Division Commander Ao Chunyuan to act on his behalf as the Commander-in-Chief. On September 5th, his younger brother Chun Guang escorted him with eleven guards in disguise, and risked passing under a wanted order with a reward of 200,000 yuan on a fishing boat to the south. On the way, they encountered adverse winds and drifted on the ocean for eight days and nights, finally arriving in Shandong on the 12th for treatment. Li eagerly hoped to recover from his injuries and return to work, and resolutely requested Dr. □ of the hospital's surgical department to perform an amputation. After two hours of discussion, permission was finally granted, and he forced his younger brother to sign the consent form. It was scheduled to amputate the diseased limb the next morning. Li knew the danger and discussed the steps for future work and arrangements for his funeral with his brother on that day. He also had the following will: "My injury is deteriorating day by day. Although amputation is now performed, it is only for the sake of one in ten thousand. If there is any misfortune, the funeral should be simple and secret, and should not affect diplomacy. The atmosphere of aggression is getting more intense and the national crisis is not over. My brother and comrades must unite sincerely and continue to struggle for final success. Then I would have sacrificed for the country and the nation, what more could I regret? This is my wish." At around 10:00 AM on the 14th, he passed away less than an hour after the operation. Chun Guang and Li's staff member Zhang Wenhuan, and others, prepared for the aftermath. The body was placed in a coffin the next afternoon. Due to the limited environment, it was hurriedly buried in □□ Mountain. When the news of Li's death came out, everyone, whether they agreed or disagreed, was shocked and mourned. Since the September 18th Incident, such a heroic sacrifice was truly the only one of its kind since the Volunteer Army rose up in arms. As for his family members, due to his anti-Japanese activities, their houses were burned to ashes and their land was confiscated. Now, his family of seven is seeking refuge in Weihai. With an elderly mother and young children, the family is impoverished and their livelihood is extremely difficult.

Grand Ceremony Welcoming Zhang Ji and Awarding the Banner in the Jiangxi Headquarters, the Central Government Awards the 34th Regiment with an Honorary Banner. Zhang Also Goes to the Front Lines to Comfort the Armies 83

Nanchang dispatch of the 9th: Central Committee member Zhang Ji brought an honorary banner to Jiangxi and awarded it to the Sixth Division, Thirty-Fourth Regiment. The banner is rectangular, about six feet high and three feet wide, with blue satin and white characters, yellow border and red tassels, embroidered with the words "Awarded by the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang," "Outstanding Achievements," "Thirty-Fourth Regiment of the Sixth Division of the National Revolutionary Army" on the left, and "October of the Republic of China, Year 22" on the right. Chairman Chiang, in accordance with the central government's award of merit, held a welcome ceremony for Zhang and an award ceremony at 10:00 AM on the 9th in the auditorium of the headquarters. Officers above the rank of school officer in the headquarters and officers of various military branches in the province attended in full military uniform. Chairman Chiang delivered a speech after the customary rituals, followed by Zhang's speech, which stated briefly: "At this critical time of internal and external troubles, we must first secure the country before resisting foreign aggression. The comrades in Jiangxi are fighting bravely against the Red bandits, doing the work of securing the country, and making heroic sacrifices. The central government is extremely concerned and is sending representatives to comfort and award them. I hope that you will take the courageous spirit of the Thirty-Fourth Regiment to eliminate the banditry and lay the foundation for the nation." Chiang's speech stated briefly: "The Thirty-Fourth Regiment, with a force of over a thousand men, resisted tens of thousands of bandits and fought for five days and nights, finally achieving victory. The merit is indeed great. Receiving an award and honorary banner from the central government is indeed a supreme honor. The central government has awarded the honorary banner once during the Huizhou campaign. It has been eight years since then, and this is the second time. Its glory is self-evident. To secure the country before resisting foreign aggression, all of our officers and soldiers must use a spirit of hardship and dedication to eliminate the communist bandits and complete the revolutionary cause, in order to repay the central government's special honor." The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

The Jiangxi Provincial Party Department and the Jiangxi Provincial Suppression Committee welcome Central Representative Zhang Ji, Jiangxi, photo by Datong Agency

At 2:00 PM, people from all walks of life held a welcome meeting for Zhang Ji at the auditorium of the Provincial Party Department. Over a thousand people attended, including leaders of various organizations and representatives from all walks of life. Li Zhongxiang presided over the meeting. After the welcoming speech, Zhang delivered a speech, mainly: (1) Explaining the significance of the central government sending a representative to Jiangxi to award the prize; (2) Stating that China, under this internal and external attack, is like a sick person fighting with others. If the disease is not cured first, the punches will be weak and how can it win? Jiangxi's Red banditry is so serious that outsiders do not know its danger. Jiangxi should arouse national attention and make a concerted effort to eliminate the Red bandits. Eliminating the bandits is tantamount to defeating Japan; (3) Banditry originated in Hunan, and most of the bandit leaders are from Hunan. Why is Jiangxi a haven for them? Because the people of Jiangxi lack a strong intellectual class, most of them flee at the first sign of trouble, so the bandits become more rampant; (4) The non-resistance policies of Zhang Xueliang and Gandhi must be completely overthrown. We hope that everyone will arouse their spirits, unite, resist, and use their own strength to relieve their own suffering. The central government has unlimited determination to suppress the bandits. We must all understand this intention and go eliminate the Red bandits before we can fight against Japan." After the meeting adjourned, the People's Consultative Council held a tea party to entertain Zhang, attended by Ouyang Wu, Peng Chengwan, and dozens of others. Ouyang reported on all the efforts made by all sectors to help the government suppress the bandits. Zhang encouraged them greatly. It is reported that Zhang will go to the front lines with Chiang within days to inspect and comfort the various troops.

Central Representative Zhang Ji and Yang, Director of the Administrative Office of the Headquarters, Yongtai, enter the venue for the welcome ceremony, photo by Jiangxi Agency, Datong Agency.

Political Dispute in Hubei Province, Provincial Party Department Requests Punishment of the Civil Affairs Director, Mediated by Central Inspectors 84

News from Hankou: Huang Danchu, the magistrate of Huangmei County, Hubei, was derelict in his duties and harmed the people. The county Party Department and various legal entities reported him. The case was referred by the Headquarters of the Three Provinces剿匪總司令部to the Provincial Party Department and the Provincial Government to notify their subordinates. After receiving the order, Civil Affairs Director Meng Guangchao immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau of the Provincial Capital to post a notice. The Provincial Party Department believed that the wording was intentionally insulting to the Party Department, violating Party discipline, undermining the rules of political tutelage, and misinterpreting the orders of the headquarters. Therefore, it was submitted for discussion at a meeting on the 8th, and three measures were decided: (1) to submit a request to the Central Government and the Nanchang Military Affairs Commission to punish the Hubei Civil Affairs Director and report the handling of the case by the Party Department; (2) to telegraph the Central Organization Committee to investigate whether Meng Guangpeng, the Hubei Provincial Government Civil Affairs Director, is a party member; (3) to send a letter to the Provincial Government ordering the Civil Affairs Department to immediately withdraw the notice. These measures were implemented separately on the 9th. At that time, Meng Guangpeng was inspecting various counties. Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun believed that the matter was a misunderstanding and should be explained urgently. It happened that Central Inspectors for the Jiangxi and Hubei provinces, Yu Xilai, arrived in Hankou from Jiangxi, and were appointed to mediate. It is reported that the following decisions were made: (1) The notice of the Public Security Bureau of the Provincial Capital will be withdrawn; (2) The Provincial Government will punish Meng Guangpeng for dereliction of duty; (3) Huang Danchu, the magistrate of Huangmei County, will be dismissed from office. The situation will not be expanded. (10th)

Zhou Lisheng Impeaches Wuhan Mayor Wu Guozhen, Huangmei County Magistrate Also Impeached 85

News from Nanjing: The Control Yuan recently approved the cases of Control Committee member Zhou Lisheng impeaching Wuhan Mayor Wu Guozhen and Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu. The impeachment documents are as follows, after being transferred to the Disciplinary Committee for review:

Impeachment of Wu Guozhen 86

Regarding the matter of impeachment: Upon investigation, Hankou Mayor Wu Guozhen, due to a report in the Hankou Pioneer Newspaper titled "The Wealthy Love Peonies," believed it was related to him. He then arrested the newspaper's president, Chen Yi, and its editor, Wang Siyuan (also known as Wang Lianshen). They were initially detained at the Public Security Bureau and later sent to the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief for the Suppression of Bandits in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui. The Headquarters, believing the matter was outside their jurisdiction, transferred them to the Hankou District Court. Chen Yi and Wang Lianshen then filed a complaint with the court. After investigation by a committee in Hankou, the facts were verified. According to Article 8 of the Provisional Constitution, people shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law. Furthermore, the National Government and the Executive Yuan have repeatedly issued instructions that all military and political organs nationwide shall not arbitrarily arrest journalists. In this case, the news published by the Pioneer Newspaper did not contain the name Wu Guozhen. The Mayor should have been unconcerned. Even if the report was inaccurate, he should have ordered a correction in accordance with the Publishing Law. Even if he considered it damaging to his personal reputation, he should have filed a lawsuit with the relevant court in accordance with the law. The Mayor neither ordered the newspaper to make corrections in accordance with the Publishing Law, nor did he file a lawsuit in court in accordance with the Code of Civil Procedure. Instead, he abused his authority and made an arbitrary arrest, and instead of sending them to the court, he sent them to the Headquarters of the Three Provinces. Had the Headquarters not considered the matter unrelated to military affairs and refused to hear the case, the Mayor would not only have violated the law, but would also have placed the Headquarters in a position of violating the law. The Mayor's actions in suppressing public opinion and trampling on human rights are not only a dereliction of duty, but also a violation of the Provisional Constitution. Therefore, in accordance with Article 2 of the Impeachment Law, this impeachment is filed, requesting that Hankou Mayor Wu Guozhen be handed over for disciplinary action to uphold the law and respect human rights. Respectfully submitted to President Ding, Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng.

Review Report, regarding the matter of reporting: The President assigned Committee Member Zhou Lisheng's impeachment case against Hankou Mayor Wu Guozhen for abusing his power and arresting the president of the Hankou Pioneer Newspaper, Chen, and its editor, Wang En-yuan. After Committee Member Zhou personally investigated the facts in Hankou, the committee members also believed that Wu Guozhen suppressed public opinion and trampled on human rights, and should be transferred for disciplinary action to uphold the law. Respectfully submitted to President Yu, Supervisory Committee Members Gao Lu, Zhu Lei, Zhang Lishi, and Jun Li-shi.

Transfer for Disciplinary Action, regarding the matter of transfer: The Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng accused Hankou Mayor Wu Guozhen of abusing his authority and making arbitrary arrests, etc. This case was assigned to Supervisory Committee Members Gao Lu, Zhu Lei, Zhang Lishi, and Li Shi-jun for review. Now, according to the report, it is believed that disciplinary action should be taken, etc. Accordingly, copies of the relevant documents are enclosed and transferred to your committee for verification and handling. This is to the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee, President Yu.

Impeachment of Huang Danchu 87

Regarding the matter of impeachment: Hubei Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu has repeatedly been accused by the county's party headquarters and mass organizations of corruption, tyranny, illegal behavior, and harming the people. Supervisor Li Sheng was assigned to investigate the matter in passing while in Hubei. After arriving in Hubei, Li Sheng immediately inquired with the Hubei Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs. According to the Provincial Department, it had previously assigned staff member Luo Guolang to conduct an on-the-spot investigation in Huangmei County. The reply stated that the accusations against the county magistrate were mostly true. Moreover, when the investigator returned to the province, the county government secretary Wang Shijie and accountant Peng Fengzhou, representing the county magistrate, privately sent a package of banknotes to the investigator, hoping for protection, etc. Such corruption, tyranny, and public bribery not only tarnish official morality but also violate criminal law. Therefore, this impeachment is filed in accordance with the law, requesting that Hubei Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu be handed over for disciplinary action. It is also requested that the Executive Yuan be consulted to order the Hubei Provincial Government to first dismiss the county magistrate from his post and hand him over to the court for custody, in order to deter corruption and preserve official conduct. Respectfully submitted to President Yu, Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng.

Review Report, regarding the matter of review: The President assigned Committee Member Zhou Lisheng's impeachment case against Hubei Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu for corruption, tyranny, and illegal behavior. After careful review, it is believed that the county magistrate's illegal activities have already been verified by an investigation conducted by the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs. This case should immediately transfer the impeached Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu for disciplinary action to rectify official conduct. Respectfully submitted to President Yu, Supervisory Committee Members Shao Hongji, Cheng Yunpeng, and Gao Lu.

Transfer for Disciplinary Action, regarding the matter of transfer: Supervisory Committee Member Zhou Lisheng accused Hubei Huangmei County Magistrate Huang Danchu of corruption, tyranny, illegal behavior, and harming the people. This case was assigned to Supervisory Committee Members Shao Hongji, Cheng Yunpeng, and Gao Lu for review. Now, according to the report, it is believed that County Magistrate Huang Danchu should be transferred for disciplinary action, etc. Accordingly, copies of the relevant documents are enclosed and transferred to your committee for verification and handling. This is to the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee, President Yu.

Changshu

Military Orders Preservation of Cannon Emplacements 92

Fushan, in this county, is located along the Yangtze River and was formerly an important military garrison. Therefore, military installations such as five cannon emplacements were established. However, they have recently been abandoned. During the January 28th Incident two years ago, the Fushan River mouth was also on the front line of defense. Therefore, the military deemed it necessary to preserve these cannon emplacements. After the war subsided, the Ministry of Military Affairs sent personnel to Changshu for inspection. They determined that the area where the emplacements were located was indeed important. Therefore, they strictly ordered the county government to protect them carefully. Now, the county has been ordered to plant forests in the surrounding open spaces of the emplacements to prevent enemy觊觎.

Eight-Year-Old Child Dies in Fire 94

The Yang Hongtai Bamboo Shop at the Jitou of the Lime Yard outside the North Gate, opened by Yang Sanbao, has been in business for over twenty years and is relatively prosperous. Because Yang is old and frail, he handed over the shop's affairs to his eldest son, Jinlong. Jinlong has five children. The two eldest sons are adults. The youngest son, Wu Bao, is only eight years old, very intelligent, and currently attends Chongshi Elementary School nearby. More than ten members of the family and shop employees lived in the back of the shop. Tragically, around midnight the night before last, a fire suddenly broke out in the bedroom at the back. Upon hearing the alarm, Jinlong immediately rescued his father Sanbao, his mother, his wife, and others. His youngest son, Wu Bao, was also in the room upstairs, crying loudly and screaming for help. However, the fire was too fierce to be rescued. After fire brigades from nearby sections drove the dragon to the scene to extinguish the fire, Wu Bao had already died in the fire. After burning for half an hour, the fire was extinguished. All the shop's buildings were destroyed, with estimated losses of over one thousand yuan. It is reported that Wu Bao suffered from eye disease and lost the use of his eyes during the fire, unable to find a window, which led to him dying in the fire.

This county's acting county magistrate, in order to raise funds to purchase equipment and prepare for winter defense, specially convened a meeting of representatives from the silver, money, salt, and local gentry industries. The salt industry will contribute 6,300 yuan, the money industry 1,500 yuan, the banks 600 yuan, and other industries 6,600 yuan. All amounts are to be paid to the county within ten days.

Water Public Security Team Uncovers Red Pill Case 100

The fourth detachment of the nineteenth team of the fifth district of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Public Security Bureau, stationed in the Dahekou area, received information that residents such as Gao Shanglin from the nearby Yangcun area were selling red pills. They raided the area at 9:00 AM on the 9th and arrested Gao Shilong from the Gao family in Gaoyou. They escorted him back to the Gao family for inspection and found more than forty catties of red pills hidden in the earthen wall in the back. They were taken back for preliminary interrogation and he confessed without hesitation. They were immediately handed over to the nineteenth team and submitted to the local bureau for disposition.

Qingjiang

Tragic Murder Case in Matou 101

Zhou Ligong, the chief gatekeeper of the Touzha in Matou Town, Huaiyin, went to the Feiyuquan bathhouse in the town to take a bath on the evening of the 7th. Two men wearing gray long gowns and speaking with a Siyang accent followed him and sat next to him. When Zhou took off his clothes to bathe, one of the two men also followed Zhou into the bath. Then he followed Zhou out to put on his clothes. Finally, the man pretended to take money, pulled out a pistol, and shot Zhou in the head. After being shot, Zhou also ran outwards. The bathhouse attendant also cried for help. The murderer then rushed to the outside of the door and shot Zhou in the waist again, killing him on the spot. All the bathers in the hall fled in terror. The murderer escaped in the chaos. Jiang Shou Peng, the head of the Sixth District Regiment, and Li Daoan, the patrol officer of the Public Security Bureau, all rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm, but were unable to apprehend the murderer. Zhou died immediately.

Journalists Association Holds Inaugural Meeting 103

Twenty-four journalists and correspondents in this county recently organized the Funing County Journalists Association. The county Party headquarters has issued a permit allowing the organization. Jiashan

Police Officer Seriously Injured in Arrest of Gamblers 104

Lu Shanyi from Shaoxing, Boai Township, Western Suburbs, lavishly celebrated his son's wedding, with guests gathering from all around. As the evening banquet ended, mahjong games were organized for entertainment. Du Keming, the police chief of the West Suburbs Public Security Bureau's branch office, learned of this and personally led several police officers to arrest the gamblers. Unexpectedly, the gamblers dared to resist arrest, surrounding and attacking the police officers. Chaos broke out. Police Chief Du's attempts to stop them were ineffective. As a result, two police officers, Jiang Jun and Wang Zisheng, were seriously injured. Police Chief Du returned to the office to report to the main bureau. Police were dispatched to arrest three of the perpetrators and hand them over to the county for investigation.

Jiaxing

Request to Reduce Education Grain Tax 105

The Jiaxing education authorities, due to a lack of funds for rural education, requested and were approved by the provincial government to collect a grain tax on fields to supplement the funding. The method is to collect two catties of grain per mu, calculated at a current market price of 2.5 cents per catty, i.e., 5 cents per mu. The county magistrate will order the township offices to collect and remit the funds. Currently, the township offices believe that the rural economy is collapsing and that farmers cannot bear the burden of the grain tax. They have filed requests for exemption. Therefore, although the early rice harvest has already begun, the tax has not been collected. It is learned that the education authorities are aware of this and plan to reduce the tax by half, collecting 2.5 cents per mu. The request is currently under review by the province. As soon as approval is granted, collection will begin.

Xiaoshan

Robbery of Fishing Boat at Sanjiangkou, One Killed 106

On the night of the 9th, two fishing boats at Sanjiangkou, while sailing to Zhanyuwei, were confronted by three pirate ships. The five fishermen were tied up. All the fish, 80 yuan in silver, and 6 large fish were robbed. When one of the fishermen shouted for help, one of the pirates fired three shots, all hitting vital points. He died immediately. The others were slightly injured. The pirates fled with the loot towards Dongjiangzui.

Economic Commission Standing Committee Member Song Ziwen Agrees to Remain in Office. Office Location Found. 111

Former Minister of Finance Song Ziwen resigned from his post and requested that the central government approve his resignation. The central government approved his resignation as Minister of Finance and Vice President of the Executive Yuan. However, the central government requested Song to remain in his position as a standing committee member of the National Economic Council. Initially, Song expressed that he needed to consider the matter before making a decision. After the presidents of the Executive Yuan and the Legislative Yuan, Wang Jingwei and Sun Ke, came to Shanghai last time to persuade him to stay, Song has agreed to continue to be responsible. Furthermore, because the former office of the old Ministry of Finance on Avenue Road was the property of the Jianghai Customs and should be returned to the Customs Administration, an estate has been found at 1729 Avenue Joffre for use as the Shanghai office of the National Economic Council. The building is currently under renovation and will soon be completed. Once it is completed, Song will be able to go to the office every day.
