Yu You Team Defeats Lux, Dong Wah Wins Against Wasces - Yu You Initially Behind by Four Goals, Then Scores Five to Four to Win - Wasces Plays with Ten Men, Dong Wah Wins Two to One - Today, Jinan Plays Against the British Navy at the Baseball Field 193

Yesterday at the baseball field, in the match between Yu You and Lux, Yu You was at a disadvantage in the first half due to facing the wind. Lux showed its might, and within half an hour, Yu You conceded four goals in a row, causing great alarm, and everyone thought they would surely lose. Unexpectedly, Yu You exerted themselves, managed to pull one goal back, and in the second half, riding the wind, their momentum soared. They scored four more goals, turning sorrow into joy with a score of five to four, snatching victory from defeat. As for the match between Yat Garden's Dong Wah and the Wasces Army, it was initially thought that with Dong Wah's Li Yichen going to Hong Kong and Guan Xun'an unable to play, Wasces' powerful force would easily defeat Dong Wah. However, the opposite happened. After Wasces scored a goal within the first minute, their right forward suddenly left the field due to a foot injury. From then on, they played with only ten men, and gaps frequently appeared in their defense, allowing Dong Wah's Cao Qiuting to score two goals in a row, leading to their final victory. It can be said that they had good fortune. Today, Jinan will play against the British Navy at the baseball field. The Navy will be represented by the very fierce Kantuo. Jinan must be careful. The China Association has a total of eight matches, and the details are listed below.

Good Fortune Shines, Dong Wah Indeed Defeats the British Army - ▲ One Goal Lost Within the First Minute ▲ Enemy General Injured, Two Goals Scored in Succession 194

After arriving in Shanghai, Wasces first drew one-to-one with Jinan, then defeated Yu You eight-to-four, and their reputation spread far and wide. Yesterday's battle with Dong Wah at Yat Garden was even more of a concern for fans. Prior to the match, public opinion considered this the only difficult hurdle for Dong Wah. Unexpectedly, good fortune shone on Dong Wah, because one quarter of an hour after the start, the army's right forward, Smith, was injured and left the field. From then on, they fought with ten men. Although they scored a goal within the first minute, Dong Wah's Cao Qiuting ultimately scored two goals in a row, resulting in a two-to-one victory. The loss of a key general greatly affected the army's strength. However, the thoroughness of Dong Wah's internal defense and the solid cooperation of the inside forwards cannot be denied. The ferocity of the Qiba center forward, Mulen, was closely monitored by Li Ning and Wang Changying, leaving him with no opportunity to move. In terms of performance, the first half was tense, and in the second half, Dong Wah attacked more than they defended. Although Wasces made a desperate effort, they achieved nothing.

▲ Dong Wah Team

Zhou Xianyan, Li Ning, Wang Changying, Tu Kaiyuan, Feng Yunyou, Wu Youliang, Wan Xianghua, Chen Hongguang, Yuan Wu, Cao Qiuting, Jia Youliang

▲ Wasces Team

Herbert, Taolewei, Shou Gedun, Wilson, S. Smith, P. Smith, Paigen, Aqiao, Mulen, Fage Tuo, Xue Bate

The City Gate Falls in an Instant 195

Dong Wah kicked off, and Tu Kaiyuan launched an attack through the center, passing the ball to the left. Wan Xianghua passed it back in front of the enemy's goal. Cao Qiuting rushed forward but was intercepted by the enemy. Feng Yunyou passed it back in, but Smith kicked it out a step ahead. The center forward received the ball, passed Wang Changying, and passed it to Paigen, reaching the baseline unimpeded. The Dong Wah goal was suddenly in danger. Paigen passed it in front of the goal, but Li Ning could not defend in time. Mulen rushed forward and kicked. The ball flew forcefully, touched Zhou Xianyan's foot, and entered the goal. In three passes, they achieved great success. Not only was Dong Wah shocked, but the audience was also amazed. Only one minute had passed. Wasces' momentum greatly increased, and the left and right wings were eager to try, constantly harassing the border. Once, Li Ning blocked the attack, and once Zhou Xianyan made a diving save, turning danger into safety.

The Goalkeeper Panics, Qiuting Achieves Success 196

Dong Wah was caught off guard and suddenly lost a goal. They had to proceed cautiously and carefully. The forward and inside forwards worked together to closely monitor the forwards who came to attack and disrupt the enemy's camp. There were wonderful passes on both wings. The enemy's defense was also strict, but the goalkeeper panicked and was restless, with the possibility of losing the goal at any time. At the same time, Wasces' right forward, P. Smith, injured his foot while fighting for the ball with Wan Xianghua and fell to the ground. From then on, they fought with only ten men. Their defensive strength greatly diminished, and their rear was increasingly unsupported, sometimes unable to attend to everything. Tu Kaiyuan's long shot once made the enemy very nervous. Wan Xianghua broke through on the east side, and the ball fell in front of the goal. Cao Qiuting headed the ball, not skillfully, but the goalkeeper was panicked and dropped the ball. The ball fell into the goal line. Dong Wah then scored a goal, tying the score at one-to-one.

Stirring Up Trouble, Another City Captured 197

From then on, Dong Wah's momentum greatly increased, and with the opposing defender missing one player, Wan Xianghua was able to move freely. Wasces' goal was like a target in front, becoming the target of everyone, and suffering the storm and being frightened. Later, Wan Xianghua sent out a corner kick. The goalkeeper rushed out to save it, but did not hit it far. However, the person fell to the ground. In the melee, Cao Qiuting shot a cold arrow from the crowd, and Dong Wah scored another goal. Afterwards, Wan sent another high ball. Cao Qiuting headed the ball six or seven yards in front of the goal, and the ball bounced off the goalkeeper's foot. He attacked again and happened to hit the goalkeeper's face. In a strange way, the ball was blocked back. It was extremely fortunate.

Loyal to the Country, All is Well 198

In the rematch, Wasces were eager for revenge, and the entire army went to the front line, fiercely attacking Dong Wah. Seeing that the situation was not good, Dong Wah defended more than attacked, resisting with all their strength. Li Ning was majestic and had merit in protecting the team. Wang Changying was loyal to the country, sparing no effort. Wu Youliang, Tu Kaiyuan, and Feng Yunyou were in harmony, and there were no flaws. Zhou Xianyan was a stalwart at the pass, invincible. Although the Qiba offensive was fierce, there was no gap to take advantage of. Although Mulai was ferocious, he was monitored and unable to do anything, wasting effort and failing at the last step. And focusing on attack, neglecting defense, he was attacked by Jia Youliang alone, directly attacking Huanglong. The city gate suddenly fell again, but it was canceled due to offside. After that, Feng Yunyou fought with injuries, and the rear was alarmed. Chen Hongguang was immediately transferred back to camp to protect the team. All was well. Two-to-one was the final result.

A Narrow Escape, Yu You Turns the Tables on Lux - Bad Luck Leads to Conceding Four Goals First - Reliance on Hard Work to Reverse the Defeat 199

The weather was pleasant and sunny. Although Yat Garden had a match, diverting many fans, there were still three thousand spectators at the baseball field. Yu You had a bad start to this season. In the first match, they were poisoned by the French team. In yesterday's battle with Lux, Jiang Shanjing's foot injury had not healed, and Aqiao was nowhere to be found. Although he followed the team, he did not play. Wang Shusen was promoted to a higher level, leaving the defense extremely empty. In the first half, they conceded four goals in a row, and the audience was uneasy, all regretting for the team. Unexpectedly, if one has ambition, things will be successful. In the second half, relying on the efforts of the generals to counterattack, they actually won five to four, turning defeat into victory. It cannot be said that this was not a narrow escape.

Shocking the World, the Heavy Defense Falls Completely 200

Lux is a team that is soft and hard. Sometimes they are as fierce as tigers, and sometimes as weak as sheep. Their cunning movements and the strangeness of their feet make people fearful. Not long after the kick-off, Hade got the ball and ran excitedly, rushing into the penalty area and hitting a goal. Yu You counterattacked twice but failed to score. Rodman tangled with Huang Ruihua at the kick-off line. Jones took the opportunity to turn behind Zhu Qiu and approach the Yu You goal. Wang Caigao was unable to save the situation. Bao Shalie arrived in an instant, puffed out his chest, and the ball had already entered the goal. Five minutes later, Bao Shalie scored another goal. The Lux offensive did not weaken slightly. Before long, Zhu Qiu again fouled in the penalty area with the courage of a strong man. Rodman took the penalty and made it four to zero.

The Iron Leg is Furious, Recapturing a City 201

At this time, the advantages and disadvantages of both sides were like a high peak and a vast sea, impossible to look up to, and the audience was also discouraged, all expecting Yu You to have no hope of recovery. Unexpectedly, the situation changed suddenly, like white clothes and gray dogs. Chen Jiaqiu was filled with righteous indignation, and with a turn of his eye, Liang Shutang was flattered and immediately gave his best performance. Jiaqiu got the ball and broke into the opponent's center defense line. Desa and the two generals greeted him side by side. Jiaqiu cleverly dodged, turned, and passed the ball to Lao Sun. With a loud bang, Robertz was caught off guard and lost a goal. The first half ended here.

The Speed of Lightning 202

In the second half, Yu You was determined to avenge their defeat. After the kick-off, Wang Shusen and Liang Shutang continued to deliver military supplies. The Lux forbidden area suddenly became restless. Kirklen made a mistake and regretted it for a lifetime. Chen Jiaqiu secretly crossed Yinping, reaching a considerable position, and passed the ball to Sun Jinrong. The two He brothers, big and small, glared angrily, bared their teeth, and came to stop him together. Sun cleverly used his divine skills, slightly adjusted his body, and left the two behind him. He drew his bow and arrow and hit the bullseye. Only two minutes had passed since the kick-off. After a long melee, Sun Jinshun made a comeback and reached the opponent's penalty area. He was embarrassed by the small He brother, so he secretly passed the ball to Li Shuoyou, who broke through the goal for the third time. The score was only one goal apart.

Yongsen and Shuoyou Achieve Success One After Another 203

At this time, Yu You's flag was extremely bright, rushing east and west, doing what they wanted. Chen Jiaqiu could not move forward, so he passed the ball to Lao Sun and advanced. The Lux rear defense was ambushed, and Sun immediately sent it to Li Shuoyou, who moved towards the goal, a foot away, creating a tie. After Li Shuoyou achieved success, he was still fierce and shouted in the east from time to time. Sun Iron Leg fought hard in the center. In the chaos, Yongsen took the opportunity to cover and kill, rushing out from the bottom of the net with the person and the ball, and then winning five to four. After that, the silver whistle blew loudly, and the Lux team returned dejectedly. Looking back at the Yu You generals, they were all elated and smiling.

Mixed Champion Qiu Feihai and Mrs. Metmore (Photo by Qichang)

▲ Yu Tianguang Fought Hard Against Lin Baohua - Lin Wins the Championship in Three Straight Sets - It's a Pity That Little Yu Lost - 丨 Six to Four · Eight to Six · Six to One 丨 207

▲ Little Yu's Skills Greatly Improved - Yu Tianguang eliminated Guo Yujie, Shi Guiyake Lasha, and Zheng Zhaojia along the way in the hard court competition, and obtained the right to compete in the final with Lin Baohua. The start is also fast, but unfortunately, when using the near ball, he used a little less force, and none of them crossed the net. His defeat to Lin Baohua is entirely a matter of experience. If given time, Little Yu's future is limitless.

▲ First Set Referee Error - The old man Gao Mei served as the referee. Yu Tianguang served, and Lin Baohua won three games in a row. Yu Tianguang tried hard to win back two games. When Lin led with four to two, Yu served in the seventh game. The first one touched the net, and then two consecutive shots went out of bounds. The score should have been forty to zero, but the referee announced that it was thirty each. The linesman Ke Lunnuofu immediately stood up to correct it, but the old man stubbornly refused to accept it and insisted on his own opinion. Ke then withdrew and protested to the committee chairman. As a result, Little Yu failed and became five to two. For a time, the audience was indignant. The chairman then discussed with Lin Yu and the referee.

▲ Singles Champions Lin Baohua and Yu Tianguang (Photo by Qichang) 208

As a result of the deliberation, the verdict was still upheld. In the next two games, Little Yu won and chased to five to four. Lin won the first set with six to four. If the referee had not made a mistake, it should have been five to five at this time, and the outcome would not have been certain.

The second set could have been won but was lost In the second set, Yu Tianguang's voice and momentum increased, taking a great advantage with four to one. Lin won back two games. In the eighth game, Yu led with forty to zero, but due to serving double faults, it became equal. As a result, Lin won, and five to three became four to four. Lin exceeded with five to four, and Yu suppressed him with strength, winning two games in a row, and chasing out with six to five. In the next game, Yu served, from a position of fifteen to forty behind, chased to equality, and then took the lead. Another point could win this set, but unfortunately Yu could not maintain his winning momentum and was won by Lin. As a result, Yu lost again with eight to six. In the last game, he had no intention of fighting, and Lin won again with six to one.

Diligence Bookstore Sells Cheap Sports Books - ▲ Preferential Treatment for Elementary School Physical Education Teachers 212

The Shanghai Diligence Bookstore has hired sports experts to publish a series of sports books, which have been praised throughout the country. Minister of Education Wang Shijie and directors of education departments in various provinces and cities have praised them highly. Recently, in accordance with the new curriculum standards, sports experts have been invited to edit physical education textbooks for all levels of elementary school, a total of twenty-five kinds, including various games such as singing, stories, recollection, imitation, competition, and so on, as well as listening to the piano, movements, singing and dancing, folk dance, imitation exercises, skill exercises, posture training, preparatory exercises, track and field, equipment exercises, and all kinds of ball games, all of which are the latest works. Elementary school teachers have an inexhaustible supply of the latest teaching materials for all levels, and the prices are low, with each kind selling for only two, three, or four angles. The teaching materials displayed by various schools at the Shanghai Municipal Elementary School Games yesterday were adopted by many and were praised by the judges. The bookstore sold them at the venue, giving teachers a preferential discount of 20%. From the 10th of this month to the end of the month, it is limited to direct mail orders from the general distribution office and the retail department. There are many buyers. In addition, the Diligence Sports Monthly published by the bookstore is edited by Shao Rugan, a sports inspector of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, and provides teaching materials for middle and elementary school teachers. The inaugural issue published on Double Ten Day has already been reprinted. The second issue, a special issue for the National Games, will be published the day after tomorrow. The third issue is a special issue for elementary school sports, priced at two angles per copy. The special price for the whole year is only one yuan and two angles, including domestic postage. Overseas, add one yuan and eight.

Citywide Boy Scout Camp Yesterday, Inspection Today: Boy Scout Headquarters Invites Pan Gongzhan to Give a Speech on Behalf of the Commander; Also Participating in the Unveiling Ceremony of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's Statue This Morning 215

The 5th Shanghai Citywide Boy Scout Grand Inspection and Camp started yesterday. Boy Scouts and Girl Scouts from various troops flocked to the downtown area. By 5:00 PM yesterday, there were 3,000 of them. The sound of loud singing on Jiangwan Road never stopped all day. Upon arriving at the campsite, the Boy Scouts from various troops set up camp in designated areas. By 6:00 PM, a white expanse had formed in front of the new City Hall, a formidable sight no less than an army marching, with a heroic spirit. At 7:30 PM, a meeting of troop leaders was held to report and discuss various precautions for the inspection and camp. At 5:30 PM, the first meeting of the Inspection and Camp Judging Committee was held at the City Boy Scout Council. This morning at 10:00 AM, after participating in the unveiling ceremony of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's statue, the grand inspection will be held. The Boy Scout Headquarters has invited Pan Gongzhan to attend and give a speech. The details are recorded as follows:

Order of Arrangement 216

The reviewing stand is erected in front of the new City Hall on Wuquan Road, facing south. A national flag is planted in the center of the field, with the band at the lower end. The surrounding area is a rectangular field, arranged in order of the troops. Each troop is divided into four squads, with the national flag at the upper end and the troop leader/instructor at the lower end. The squad leader stands in front of the squad members, to the right of the instructor. The campsites are set up in the outer circle, also arranged according to the order of the council's regulations.

Start of Camping 217

The uniform is prescribed as khaki wool coat and hat, black shoes, and the badge issued by the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts. Each troop brings one troop flag, four squad flags, and batons for each troop member, led by the troop leader or instructor. At least eighteen people participate from each troop. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the energetic athletes from various troops marched to their destination and began to set up camp. The military appearance was orderly and well-organized.

Camping Order 218

November 11th (Camping): Registration starts at 10:00 AM, registration deadline at 5:00 PM, guarding starts at 5:30 PM, dinner at 6:30 PM, troop leader meeting at 7:00 PM, various troops automatic games or assignments at 8:00 PM, lights out at 9:30 PM (Inspection): Wake up at 6:00 AM, wash and tidy up clothes, clean up camp at 6:30 AM, breakfast at 7:00 AM, participate in the unveiling of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's statue, inspection registration, lunch after the inspection at 11:00 AM, performance preparation at 1:00 PM, performance starts at 1:30 PM, flag down at 6:00 PM, dinner at 6:30 PM, campfire party at 7:10 PM, lights out at 9:30 PM, November 13th, wake up at 6:00 AM, wash and tidy clothes, breakfast at 7:00 AM, clean up camp at 7:40 AM, awards at 9:30 AM, lunch at 11:30 AM, dismantling the camp at 12:00 PM.

Today's Inspection 219

This morning at 10:00 AM, all Boy Scouts will participate in the inauguration ceremony of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's statue. They must report before 9:00 AM. After the ceremony, they will enter the field to hold the Grand Inspection. Central representatives, Mayor Wu, Director Pan, and Committee Member Tong will all be present for the inspection. The inspection order is as follows: (1) Enter the field (Qin music), (2) Raise the flag, (3) Sing the Party Song, (4) Pay the highest respects to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-Sen, (5) Read Dr. Sun Yat-Sen's will, (6) Three minutes of silence, (7) Inspection ceremony, (8) Report, (9) Speech, (10) Sing the Boy Scout Song, (11) Cheer, (12) Ceremony completed (play music).

Invitation to Attend 220

The Boy Scout Council has sent letters to various organizations, institutions, and sectors to visit the inspection ceremony, saying that the inspection ceremony will be held at 11:00 AM on November 12th, and you are cordially invited to attend and provide guidance. Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, and Tong Xingbai, Chairman of the Preparatory Committee for the 5th Shanghai City Chinese Boy Scout Grand Inspection and Camp, Location: Wuquan Road, Shanghai Jiangwan Central District, the headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scout command has telegraphed Mr. Pan Gongzhan's representative to attend and give a speech.

Annual Meeting of the Geological Society 221

(Beijing, November 11th) The annual meeting of the Geological Society of China opened this morning at the Tsinghua Biological Museum. In the afternoon, they will go to Yenching University to read joint members' papers.

Jiangsu Provincial Schools' September Expenses Have Been Signed 222

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Fund Management Office has issued the expenses for the month of August (the first half of August and the second half of September for social education institutions and vocational schools, while the expenses for September are issued for rural teachers' schools and experimental elementary schools or affiliated elementary schools) in October. It is reported that the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office held an audit committee meeting on the afternoon of the 10th of this month, and the notification of funds for the month of September for provincial middle schools and normal schools has been signed (social education institutions and vocational schools, rural normal schools and experimental elementary schools) Affiliated elementary schools, etc., are analogized according to the examples and signed separately for September and October) After submission to the Education Department for sealing and other procedures, the notices can be filled out and sent to the schools separately. It is also reported that the Education Treasury currently has only 10,000 to 20,000 in savings. The Management Office has issued separate orders to the superintendents of various counties to step up the recovery of funds, and has dispatched special commissioners to various counties to collect funds, so as to raise enough education funds to issue the September expenses for provincial schools and the October expenses for rural teachers and elementary schools.

Spring and Autumn Special Issue - Eating

The Problem of Eating 224

— Ziyin

Eating rice fills the stomach, and being full gives you energy. With energy, you can work hard and get things done. This sequence of events has been around since the beginning of time, since Shennong invented the cultivation of grains, right? Thinking about it carefully, it's indeed quite interesting. Now, with European and American influences sweeping across China, some fashionable people have changed their habits and are eating bread. Thus, the problem of eating rice has transformed into the problem of eating bread. If you meet an unemployed friend, you might talk about how to solve the bread problem. Instead of talking about the Europeanized bread problem, it would be more accurate to talk about the purely domestic problem of eating rice.

Shanghai, in the eyes of friends in the interior, is truly the easiest place to find food. However, the opposite is true. Shanghai is arguably the most difficult place to find food. If you don't believe me, I can provide concrete examples. Suppose a company—the word "company" is a general term; renting a living room can also be called a company—or a school—which is explained in the same way as a company—wants to hire one or two people. They place a small advertisement with three or four lines of twenty characters. Our general population, eager to find food, will travel thousands of miles to search for it, without asking whether their qualifications are sufficient or their experience is adequate. They rashly go to take the exam, and as a result, they fail miserably, and most are eliminated. From then on, they have no choice but to wait for the second opportunity to come. Day after day, they buy newspapers, and when they see advertisements like "hiring" or "seeking," they won't make a mistake again. Once, twice, three times, four times, going on like this, and in the end, they remain the same. Some people who come from the interior have relatives and friends in Shanghai, so they can still rely on them; some who come to Shanghai and don't know anyone rent apartments and pay for meals. When the money they brought runs out, they end up jumping into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. Can you imagine how tragic that is? Thinking this way, finding food in Shanghai is more difficult than in the interior. However, there is a group of people who can eat all kinds of delicacies without spending money. This group of people is respectfully called "beggars" by the Shanghainese. Beggars also have factions. For example, the beggars on Sanma Road and the beggars on Sima Road don't interfere with each other. They each have their own territory and their own sources. After the standard lunch or dinner time, the beggars go out with broken bowls and paper bags, waiting in their respective alleys or intersections. The cooks of the restaurants transfer the leftovers from the diners, and they seem to have a rule that they only need to step forward and pour it out. In this way, they can eat without working. It is said that there are even some old hands in this business who can't finish the food they get, so they soak it in boiling water and sell it to rickshaw pullers for snacks at twenty coppers a bowl! These beggars can be considered economists.

It is difficult for the very rich to approach and understand how they live, but ideally, there shouldn't be much difference. Since it's not relevant to this article, I won't discuss it. Middle- and upper-class families are often accessible, so I know a little about them. Their lives are relatively comfortable. The so-called housewives have the title of housewife but not the reality. All the trivial household affairs are entrusted to the children's nannies and the cleaning maids. People who eat other people's food are never entirely well-intentioned. They often throw good rice and leftover dishes into the sewers. This kind of waste, although it won't be struck by lightning as superstitious people believe, I think it's still hard on one's conscience.

For friends on the verge of desperation, trying to find a bowl of rice is as difficult as described above, while for another type of people, eating is so easy. This is truly a great inequality among human beings!

People in the interior say that "it's easy to find food in Shanghai," which probably refers to the servants of middle- and upper-class families and those beggars, but it can't be taken as a universally true statement.

Special Foods of Guizhou 225

— Tan Wenbing

Guizhou is a province in the southwest, covered with mountains. It is considered one of the poorest places in inland China. However, Guizhou has many special products that are not easily found in other provinces. I will briefly describe one or two of them to inform the readers:

▲Giant Salamander In the rivers around Guiyang, Guizhou, in addition to common carp and crucian carp, there is a special product called the "baby" (note 1) fish. This fish is an amphibian, and its shape is completely like a human, with hands and feet, able to stand and sit, with eyes, ears, mouth, and nose on its head, scales on its body, and a fish mouth. It has gills under its jaw for breathing in water. The larger ones are one or two feet long and cry just like a newborn baby, so they are called "baby fish." They are most easily seen in the summer. When the sun sets, they climb ashore in groups, sitting or standing, crying or wailing. From a distance, they look like naked children. However, they are very clever. When they see people coming, they dive into the water, so they are not easy to catch. However, sometimes they are caught by fishermen and sold in the market. Cruel people want to taste exotic flavors and still treat them as ordinary fish, killing and eating them. Their taste is very fresh, but if they are not cooked properly, they will taste fishy and difficult to eat. If they are lucky, they will meet kind people who not only don't have the heart to eat them but also make a gold earring for them, wear it on their ears as a mark, and then release them back into the river. In the future, when fishermen encounter them, they will no longer catch them.

▲Luohu Chili Peppers Chili peppers are available everywhere, but the Luohu (note 2) chili peppers of Guizhou are different from ordinary ones. Because ordinary chili peppers are annual herbaceous plants, while the Luohu chili peppers of Guizhou grow on large trees. Their taste is not only better than ordinary chili peppers, but no matter what kind of dish, as long as you add Luohu chili peppers, they can be preserved for more than ten days even in the hot summer without spoiling. Therefore, ordinary chili peppers cost only a few hundred cash per catty, while Luohu chili peppers cost at least one or two yuan per catty. However, they are produced in Luohu County, Guizhou. They cannot be transplanted to other places, probably because the people of Guizhou are addicted to chili peppers. They cannot be full without chili peppers, so the Creator specially created this plant to bestow upon them!

There are many other special products, but due to limited space, I will talk about them next time if I have the opportunity.

(Note 1) Baby - In Guizhou, people call children babies.

(Note 2) Luohu - A place name, a county in Guizhou.

Chinese Food in Paris 226

— Zhu Mei, From Paris

Naturally, my first meal in Paris was Chinese food at a Chinese restaurant. I had planned this on the ship in advance. I was really getting tired of eating bread every day, so eating Chinese food was a happy event. There are several Chinese restaurants in Paris: Tianjin, Dongfang, Wanhualou, Zhonghualou, Shanghailou, and Beijing Restaurant. There are also three near Paris in the suburb of Bignoux. The restaurants are about the same size except Wanhualou, which is the largest and owned by Cantonese people. The owner of Tianjin Restaurant is a French woman who used to be the wife of Lao Xiao. Almost all students who studied in Europe knew Lao Xiao. He made a lot of money from running the restaurant, but the French woman took it all. She divorced him, and he later went to work as a cook at another restaurant. Almost all the Chinese restaurants use Chinese servants, except for Zhonghualou, which uses a few French people. The Chinese restaurants are mostly frequented by Chinese students, followed by many foreigners.

Eating in Changshu 227

— Yu Youqing

Changshu's soy sauce chicken has become a delicacy for the people of Suzhou. There are many branches in Guanqian Street in Suzhou, such as Longfengzhai and Ma Yongzhai, which seem to compete with Cai Yanzhai's watermelon seeds. In the eyes of us Changshu people, besides soy sauce chicken and soy sauce meat, there are many other special products, such as the golden claw crabs of Tantang, which are no less than those produced in Yangcheng Lake. The shrimp in the Dahe River have soft and thin shells. After the plum rain season, they are full of eggs, which other places cannot match. The sea white shrimp in the Yangtze River have an even more delicious taste. The honey peaches of Guli Village, the deep-water water chestnuts of Caojing, the cantaloupe of Hengjing, the watermelon of Xuegou, and the fresh hairy chestnuts of Dingshan. The white bayberries of Baoyan are all delicacies among fruits. People from other places probably don't know about them, so they are not well-known. On fine spring days, it is a pleasure to visit the mountains in groups and taste the dried tofu in front of the mountain outside the West Gate and the purple ripe water chestnuts outside the North Gate. This is what people who visit Mount Yu often talk about. The fragrant japonica rice and blood glutinous rice are also special products of Changshu. It is said that in the late Qing Dynasty, they were used as tribute. Unfortunately, the production of blood glutinous rice has been decreasing day by day. There are countless other snacks, probably the same as in other places.

Nowadays, the most famous special products of Changshu are probably the soy sauce chicken and soy sauce meat of Ma Yongzhai. As far as I know, the soy sauce chicken of Yanmu Town in Wujiang is no less than that of Changshu, but unfortunately, no one is promoting it. Otherwise, it could be called comparable to the hoof of Fengjing Town. Compared to other places, eating in Changshu's restaurants is better than in Suzhou and Shanghai. Therefore, people like Yu Saoxin and Kang Nanhai used to often visit Mount Yu.

Liangxiang Chestnuts and Coincidence 228

— Shi Jihong

There's a common saying among Shanghai people: "Liangxiang chestnuts, hard times ahead." Coincidentally, this year, Liangxiang chestnut stalls are everywhere, overflowing. Coincidentally, this year, times are truly harder than in previous years, with an economic downturn. The rich have money but nowhere to spend it, the poor need money but have no way to get it. A simple saying has actually become a prophecy: the more Liangxiang chestnuts there are, the harder people's lives become.

Coincidentally, Shanghai people are inventive. Just eating chestnuts isn't enough, they have to be candied and stir-fried. Having a phonograph at the stall isn't lively enough, they have to have four-tube or five-tube radios. Costs increase, profits decrease. Liangxiang chestnuts, hard times ahead—another omen.

Usually, a bag of chestnuts costs four cents of silver, equal to twelve copper coins. But coincidentally, this year the price hasn't increased. What's more, they're even doing a "buy two bags, get one free" promotion. Although the quantity isn't increased, "Liangxiang chestnuts, hard times ahead" adds another clear symbol. Otherwise, if business were good, everyone would be raising prices, let alone offering a "buy two, get one free" deal?

The word "difficult," according to Napoleon, exists only in the dictionary of fools. Of course! Our money is flowing out one coin at a time because we lack the ability to succeed; therefore, we have this saying, "Liangxiang chestnuts, hard times ahead."

The Record of Crabs 229

— Qing Qu

The types of crabs, if studied, are a very interesting thing. However, people who enjoy holding crabs only chew them heartily, unaware that their origin and region are closely related! The typical gourmets by the sea know that when "green crabs" (that is, Charybdis japonica) come onto the market in June and July, they come from Zhenning, Zhejiang, and live in the mudflats, revered as the best. But only one or two Western restaurants treat them as rare commodities, and they aren't tasted at ordinary, common banquets. The large "green crabs" can be a foot in circumference, and their two large pincers are especially swollen and fat. The strength of their claws is often enough to cut off a person's finger. When they are cooked in a pot and placed on a white porcelain plate, the color is especially crimson, like red coral, quite a sight to behold! Thirty years ago, when the Guang Bang in Shanghai held the Ullambana Festival, they were used as the most valuable offering to the gods. If you used them as snacks with wine, only someone as rich and discerning as Yan Xiaofang would dare to indulge. Later, Qing Daoren was also a famous crab eater. In fact, the old man was very frugal and still thought "green crabs" were too expensive, unwilling to spend the money to satisfy his appetite!

The Shanghai market mostly uses "Yangcheng Lake crabs" as a selling point, because this type of crab is the most abundant, and the crab bodies seem to be larger than others, with females weighing more than a pound. But this is merely appearance, the contents and cream are not necessarily exquisite. If you carefully distinguish, you will know that they cannot compare to the crabs you encounter in the fishing nets in the countryside! In the southeast of Jiading, there is a kind called "Wang Zi crab" and "Gong Zi crab," which are the most famous. Unfortunately, the output is relatively small, and they are not easily caught until the late autumn weather. What makes these crabs recognizable is that on the back of their shells, there are clearly two types, "Wang" and "Gong." If you don't believe it, put them in a pot and mix them with other crabs of equal size. When they are cooked, lift the lid and you will see that the "Wang" and "Gong" characters are always on top, while the other crabs are pressed underneath. This is the most obvious example. Therefore, the firmness and fullness of this kind of crab can be seen in the amount of struggling strength at the point of death, and the price is more precious!

Now, almost all crabs have "emerged" (a colloquialism meaning there are many crabs), but these two kinds of crabs have not yet appeared on the market. "Zhangpu crabs" from the west gate countryside are the latest to appear. The crab bodies are smaller, but the legs are longer, and the hairs on the legs are slightly yellow. An old person who is familiar with the origin and history of crabs can tell at a glance. There is a Mr. Gu, named Futing, who is nearly eighty years old this year. He has a lifelong addiction to eating crabs. His family always has crabs raised in tanks. If he thinks of eating them, he can take them at will and satisfy his crab craving without having to go out and look for them at expensive prices. He is truly considered an expert in eating crabs! Someone went to ask him where he got his crabs. He never said. Even in the season when there are no crabs to chew on, if you bring up the word "crab," he will reply, "I have them! I have them!" His way of eating crabs is also different from others. Sometimes, in a tavern, he would first break off the pincers of a crab and chew on them one by one. By the time he was tipsy, there would still be a pile of the crab body (slang) untouched. After drinking, he would take it home. He would only finish his crab-eating work during dinner. This way of eating can be considered the most economical plan. I greatly admire him, and I must write it out today for the benefit of like-minded people!

Eating in Suzhou 230

— Bingqian

Seven or eight years ago, around the time when maple leaves were turning red and osmanthus flowers were fragrant, I went to Hangzhou to study, staying by the mountains and facing the water. A classmate from Suzhou brought some local specialties to school and generously shared them. After enjoying the food, I quickly wrote a short article called "Eating in Suzhou," which was published in the Qingguang column of the Shishi Xinbao newspaper. A friend from Guangdong, whose name I have already forgotten, insisted that eating in Guangzhou was better and had a written argument with me. In the end, he arrogantly presented a Guangdong mooncake that cost more than one hundred yuan and asked if I, a poor student, had ever tasted one. I said that was capitalized eating, how could it be compared to the people-oriented eating in Suzhou? The debate finally came to an end. Years have passed, it feels like yesterday. I never dreamed that I would wander to the beautiful and culturally rich Suzhou. I am truly fortunate. In the past, eating was just something I talked about on paper, but now, like working in a chemistry lab, I can actually experiment!

Originally, clothing, food, housing, and transportation are essential elements in our daily lives. If we analyze life in detail, who doesn't strive for clothing and food? To put it more broadly, aren't world panic, economic recession, and bread problems also major reasons?

Even the sages said, "Food and sex are human nature." From the moment a person is born until the moment they die, they cannot separate from the word "food" for even one day, unless they are sick. "Three days without food will lead to hunger, seven days without food will lead to death," is a well-established conclusion. Therefore, when I talk about "eating," I don't think the general moralists will regard me as a glutton, right?

Suzhou is a land of fish and rice, a blessed paradise, so the food here is slightly better than in other places. When you walk into the bustling Xuanmiao Temple, you will smell the strong aroma of five spices and scallions. There is Yiwai Zhai's pork chop, with sweet and sour, pepper and salt flavors, pleasing and delicious, all up to you. There is Wufang Zhai's doufu soup, which, according to hygiene principles, is the most nutritious. However, mentioning doufu soup always makes people have a slightly bitter aftertaste. The first time I went to Xuanmiao Temple with a local colleague, he first suggested going to eat doufu soup. I was very surprised and wondered what was so delicious about doufu soup? After trying it, I felt that it had a different flavor. The soup is mixed with dried shrimp, seaweed skin, sesame oil, chili, vinegar, soy sauce… "Five flavors harmonizing create a hundred flavors fragrance." We ate it smoothly and ordered another bowl. Each bowl costs only sixteen copper coins, which can be said to be cheap and good. Then there are also steamed crab dumplings with steaming air, oily black fish, and evenly thick lotus root powder, which are quite tempting. In the crowd, there are people selling pear paste candy, with the soft, delicate Wu dialect, which is enough to make people stop. As for whether the candy is delicious or not? I have not tasted it. The rest of the scattered stalls and shops are arranged in a complex manner, simply a collection of snacks.

Suzhou's sweets are not me doing free promotion for them, they are already famous far and wide. When the League of Nations investigation team visited our country, didn't they come to Suzhou specifically to purchase sweets? The entrances of the candy stores are lined with many small cabinets and colored glass bottles, like opening an exhibition, with various colors and numerous varieties. They have great magic for people, especially children who regard candy as their second life. What chocolate, Gu Keli… are not something we can touch. Under the circumstances of "wanting the horse to run fast, but not wanting the horse to eat grass," what I like the most is butter pine nut candy. The outside of the candy is wrapped in clean and transparent cellophane. When you eat it, it is fresh, sweet, and palatable, and the pine nuts also have the benefit of "prolonging life." Only Suzhou has it, and I especially introduce it to the readers.

Eating in a teahouse is even more people-oriented. A bag of watermelon seeds for a few copper coins can pass a lot of time. There are also several types, such as licorice, perfume, rose… etc. They are small and crispy, so when you eat them, it is different from ordinary wide-backed watermelon seeds or giant watermelon seeds, and you need a bit of eating art! There are also five-spice beans, green plums, olives… sprinkled with licorice powder… interspersed with some peeling sounds while talking and laughing, which is also a unique teahouse style in Suzhou!

The season is autumn. At the entrances of the fruit stores, there are sugar chestnut frying pans. On the streets and alleys, there are vendors selling cooked water chestnuts and fat Yangcheng Lake crabs, and carts of stir-fried ginkgo can be seen everywhere. Sitting at home, without having to move your feet, you can get delicious food. Only the paradise of Suzhou can be enjoyed.

As for Lugaojian's braised pork and Pan Wansheng's fermented bean curd, they were both tributes from the past and are now delicacies. The other delicious things are really too numerous to count!

Thinking of Guangdong's mooncakes that cost more than one hundred yuan and the aristocratic eating of "spending ten thousand coins on food and still having nothing to eat," what is the difference? From the perspective of a foreigner living here, eating in Suzhou is definitely worthy of the name!

Free Talk

The Secret to Success for Writers 231

— Zhongfang

I once saw in a notebook that Shi Nai'an first hung portraits of the thirty-six main characters of the Water Margin in his study, looking at them morning and night. Later, he "understood them spiritually," and when he wrote, it was as if he had "divine help," so the thirty-six people became active on paper.

This is one of our Chinese ancestral "secrets" for the success of writers. Today, after several studies of the Water Margin, it has been determined that it was not the individual creation of someone named Shi Nai'an, but the fruit of accumulated folk legends. The so-called personalities of the thirty-six main characters were not derived by Shi Nai'an from studying the portraits, but were successfully molded by many unknown folk artists. Shi Nai'an only did the final compilation, so the "secret to success" passed down in the notebook is self-defeating and becomes one of countless "forced interpretations."

In our ancestral "secrets to success," there is another one. The famous Sima Qian was the creator or successful experimenter of this "secret." This means that the reason Sima Qian's writing was "not clumsy and straightforward" was because he "traveled around famous mountains and rivers." In ancient China, where transportation was inconvenient, "traveling around famous mountains and rivers" was indeed not something most people could do. However, Sima Qian actually "traveled" and his writing turned out to be extraordinary, so this "secret" is trustworthy. "Famous mountains and rivers," these dead things—no, it should be said "beautiful nature"—may be able to give a poet a few more poems, or even make a poet's work more "rich and strange," like Du Fu after entering Shu, but it is truly difficult to understand how the prose writer Sima Qian could also get help from "famous mountains and rivers" in his annals and biographies, which were like fragmented court reports. When some ancient Chinese "critics" talked about the "fluency" or "goodness" of writing, they always said things like "understand it spiritually." The saying of "famous mountains and rivers" should also be a kind of "understanding it spiritually." Anyway, it has been "long determined" that a complete Records of the Grand Historian contains all kinds of writing methods.

Jin Shengtan was much more straightforward. He judged that the Water Margin learned from Sima Qian's writing style. This "discovery" of his is actually the third type of Chinese ancestral writer's "secret to success," namely the so-called "transformation." Mr. Shi Zhicun translated it into "modern language," which is "every writer must borrow from the literature of his ancestors." Needless to say, hanging portraits in the study and looking at them morning and night is too troublesome, and you have to ask someone to paint the portraits first, which is especially troublesome. As for "famous mountains and rivers," although "water and land joint transportation" and the opening of highways have made it seem much more convenient than in Sima Qian's time, it is still quite annoying to travel around. It is better to sit comfortably in the study and "borrow from the previous generation." A lithographic edition of Zhuangzi and a lithographic edition of Wen Xuan cost at most four dollars, saving both money and time. With this comparison, it can be seen that those who firmly advise young people to first seek rich life experience are really incredibly silly.

Cloth Peddler 232

— He Jiahui

Shaking a small flower drum, the cloth peddler walks from village to village, from house to house.

"...Teng teng teng... buy cloth, buy cloth... Teng teng teng... there are so many goods today... Teng teng teng..."

Putting down the load on his shoulders, he shouted loudly, panting. He was very familiar with these places, and he was very familiar with the girls in this area. Just don't know their names. The houses in the countryside are very strange. If several houses are together, there is always a very, very large public yard. In this yard, no matter what season it is, you can see cow dung, chicken dung all over the ground, and diapers floating in the air.

While shaking the small drum in the yard, he chose a stool to sit down and waited for customers. Needless to say, these customers are all girls. As soon as they hear his voice, they always immediately stick their heads out of the lattice windows upstairs and lean over to greet him:

"Hey, cloth seller, let us see your new patterns!"

Then he heard the sound of rolling stones, as the impatient girls came down from the stairs of each house and surrounded the load. His load has many drawers, and they have to rummage through these drawers every time, looking at all the silk threads, lace, pins, buttons, and all the odds and ends. As for the cloth, that goes without saying. They not only have to look at it carefully, but also examine each piece separately. "These patterns are just coming into fashion!"

"No, that's already out of date. My sister bought it last year."

"It looks good, but it's not durable. It feels as thin as paper."

"Reduce the price, I really want to buy a few feet丨丨"

They flipped the cloth back and forth, noisy, like children at the entrance of a candy store. Those sharp eyes all fell on his face, as if exploring, trying to grasp his business weaknesses and attack him.

They are all young, lively girls, as bright as the sun in the countryside. But strangely, they all have stingy minds and cunning tricks, and they want to take advantage of even a small amount of money.

"How many cents a foot?"

"Who wants something that's so frighteningly expensive!"

"Hey, wouldn't it be much cheaper to buy it in the city?"

Women's mouths are really scary. They don't care if people lose money or not, they just want to reduce the price, as if they would only be satisfied if they reduced it to nothing and gave it to them for free.

"Okay, I'll give you a few more cents!"

He looked around, looked at those bright, cunning faces, and helplessly? replied with a wry smile.

"You have to take off a little more!"

"I also have to spend money to buy it, and I also have to spend my energy丨丨丨"

Although he said it so gently, and made concessions to the point where he could no longer give in, those heartless girls were still not satisfied;

"People who do business always say the same thing, all the talk about losing money is false. If you don't take off a little more, we won't buy it." "Losing money is true, I'm being honest, but of course old customers can get a little more length."

After a long argument, the business was finally settled, but it was even more troublesome when measuring the cloth.

"Give me a little more, give me a little more, you said yourself that the length is enough!"

"Giving so" little, it's really deceiving!"

They scrambled to press their hands on the cloth, following his ruler closely, specifying a large extra piece of cloth, asking him to give it away, otherwise they would take his ruler and not let go. Of course, he didn't want to at first, after all, it wasn't a Beijing goods store, where could he give away so much? But in the end, he couldn't outwit these girls and had to be careless. Although this kind of transaction clearly didn't make any money, and his own energy was clearly wasted, what else could he do if he didn't do this?

Watching those satisfied girls disperse in a swarm. He just shook his head sadly and mournfully.

When he entered this yard, it may have been in the morning, or it may have been at noon, but he always went back near dusk. Sometimes bathed in the setting sun, sometimes drenched in heavy rain, and sometimes braving the snow, this poor cloth peddler, shaking his drum, carrying a heavy load of cloth, trudging home with tired steps.

"I'm so tired all day, but I only sold this little money, is it enough to eat and wear?" On the way back, he might put the load in a broken pavilion or an old temple, counting the day's income and sighing.

Literary Miscellany 233

—

(One)

In Wei Jinzhi's recently published novel "White Flag Bearer," I saw a few sentences about "birds in the free sky." He said that everyone envies the birds flying in the sky, but birds, in reality, are not as free as they imagine. He critically explained the psychology of the protagonist who is working, saying:

Usually, he dreams about it, and with the heart of a poet, he appreciates the eagles in the sky, looking up and admiring them as they are set off against the vast sky. Flying freely, chirping like new jingle bells, but not knowing that the flying is for foraging and the chirping is for hunger. The whip of real life awakens poets from such dreams, of course, quite a few, but at present, there are still many people who think this way. Therefore, I am quoting these two sentences from "White Flag Bearer" again. Poets, don't dream and write about the soaring of "geese" anymore. You can further investigate the reasons and troubles for their soaring. Like humans, aren't birds also struggling for survival?

(Two)

Shen Congwen, in the preface to "A Mother," which was recently published, wrote a preface explaining his own creative attitude. The first paragraph begins by saying:

Because of the troubles of survival, I feel that writing about male and female relationships is more suitable than writing other articles. When writing this, my attitude is no different from my usual creative attitude. In the conflict caused by the desire of men and women, I only do my best to observe and explain this inevitable change. I do not add any prejudiced opinions in favor of or protecting any of the characters, and it seems that I should not have this is the author's very faithful confession of his creative attitude, an attitude that a former realist writer would inevitably adopt. However, the problem lies here. Is it true that the author has no "preconceived notions" when writing? This is impossible. Take photography, for example. It seems that there is no "preconceived notion" and it is "objective and realistic," but the position of the characters and the angle of the light always express the photographer's philosophy. There are "preconceived notions." Of course, the same is true for novels.

(Three)

Let's talk about Li Jinming's creative attitude again. In his recently published collection of novels, "Lost Scenery," he also wrote a self-confession of his creative attitude, a preface. He criticized his own thinking and further explained:

My attitude is the attitude of a passerby. The so-called passerby is detached from hope, but looks down on complacency, reaction, and decadence; in other words, my obligation is only to point out the shortcomings of certain things. And the intention is, of course, to hope that the good aspects are more numerous.

This is of course also an understanding of old realism, but he is one step further than Shen Congwen. Although "my obligation is to point out the shortcomings of certain things," he understands that there are "preconceived notions" in this. In fact, a writer "without preconceived notions"

Two Brothers (26) 234

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

"He's really a very handsome man."

"Do you think so?"

"Of course, and he seems like a happy person."

What strange demand made him suddenly tell the barmaid about Zhe'an receiving the inheritance? Why did this thought, which he didn't want to think about when he was alone, which he rejected because he was afraid of disturbing himself, run to his lips at this time? And why was he willing to let this thought run out of his lips, as if he needed to pour out his bitter heart again in front of something?

He said, putting one leg over the other:

"My brother is very lucky, he recently inherited an inheritance with an income of 20,000 francs a year."

She opened her blue, greedy eyes wide and said:

"Ah! But who gave him this inheritance? His grandmother, or his aunt?"

"Not at all, it was a friend of our family."

"Just a friend? That's impossible! And he didn't leave anything for you?"

"No. I'm not very familiar with this person."

She thought for a while, then a strange smile floated on her lips:

"Then! Your brother is fortunate to have this kind of friend! Really, no wonder he's not like you at all!"

He wanted to slap her, for reasons that he himself didn't understand. His mouth twitched and asked her:

"What do you mean by that?"

She looked stupid and innocent:

"Me, nothing. I mean he has better opportunities than you."

He threw a lang on the table and left.

Now he silently repeated the sentence: "No wonder he's not like you at all."

What was she thinking, what was the hidden meaning in her words! There must be some cunning, malice, and humiliation in it. That's right, the girl must think Zhe'an is Maraisa's son.

Thinking that people suspected his mother's chastity, he was so moved that he stopped and looked around, wanting to find a place to sit down.

There was another coffee shop opposite him. He walked in, grabbed a chair and sat down. When the waiter ran over and asked him what he wanted, he replied, "A beer."

He felt his heart beating very hard: a chill ran down his skin in waves. Suddenly he remembered Malosco's words last night: "This will not end well." Did he and this low-class girl have the same thoughts, the same suspicions?

US Cotton is Firm Due to Weak US Dollar 249

New York, November 10th, reports on the condition of the cotton market over the past two weeks, saying that the government's cotton production report on the 3rd estimated a lower harvest than the average private estimate, so past transactions revealed a disappearance of uncertain weather. The cotton market had concluded a lot when the report numbers were released, and the price then rose. Due to the weakness of the US dollar and the step-by-step rise in gold prices, buying interest became stronger, and this phenomenon obviously revived talk of currency expansion. Buyers were even more excited by the firmness of the wheat market and the securities market. It is heard that farmers are hoarding cotton with the help of government loans, and that there are currently many farmers receiving loans in the next year's program to limit cotton fields to help with this. Recent cold and rain have delayed the listing of new cotton and damaged the cotton left in the fields. At the same time, the morale of many parties is quite strong, based on the decline of the US dollar and the cotton hoarding movement in the South. There are also some parties who do not want to buy in large quantities following the buying trend, because they want to wait for the future development of the business situation.

The Situation of China Tea Exports to Various Countries in the First Ten Months of This Year | Increased Compared to the Same Period Last Year | 254

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry has consistently published statistics on the export of China tea, which has been well-received by tea industry professionals. Recently, the bureau released a comparison of China tea trade to various countries from January to October of this year with the same period last year to observe the growth and decline of China tea trade over the two years. According to the bureau, the quantity of black tea, green tea, brick tea, and other teas this year has significantly increased compared to the same period last year, with a total increase of 118,851 dan and 98 jin. By tea type, green tea increased by 36,945 dan and 47 jin, black tea increased by 32,909 dan and 9 jin, but these were all black teas exported from Hankou in the Hubei and Hunan provinces. The renowned Keemun black tea saw a decrease in exports compared to last year. Brick tea increased by 32,067 dan and 47 jin, all exported from Hankou to Russia. Other teas also increased by 16,929 dan and 95 jin. By country, Russia saw the largest increase, with 56,615 dan and 95 jin. The United States followed, with 21,783 dan and 91 jin. Other increases included the United Kingdom with 16,657 dan and 97 jin, Africa with 6,212 dan and 88 jin, India with 3,224 dan and 29 jin, and other countries with a combined increase of 17,733 dan and 31 jin. However, sales to France decreased by 3,376 dan and 33 jin compared to last year. In Russia, the largest increase was in brick tea, with 31,739 dan and 26 jin, followed by black tea with 13,358 dan and 50 jin, and then green tea with 4,717 dan and 36 jin. Other teas also increased by 6,800 dan and 83 jin. In the United States, both black and green tea increased by over 10,000 dan. Exports of black tea to the UK increased by over 7,000 dan, all from Hubei and Hunan. Other teas also increased by over 8,000 dan. In Africa, green tea increased by 16,719 dan and 52 jin, but black tea decreased by 10,497 dan and 21 jin. India also showed a trend of increasing green tea and decreasing black tea. Other countries saw a larger increase in black tea. (Table omitted)

Amateur Musings

An Important Matter That the Industrial and Commercial Sectors Should Pay Attention To 256

— Gong Pu

Many of the readers of this publication are friends in the industrial and commercial sectors. The reporter feels that the industrial and commercial sectors have recently discovered an important matter. I wonder if people in these sectors have paid close attention to it? That is the issue of domestic sales of Chinese goods actually encountering opposition from Chinese people. Observing the dispute between the Zhuangke (lodging agents) of the Sanshan Guildhall in Shanghai, established by Fujian merchants, and the Chinese National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, as well as the news of Xuzhou merchants preventing the National Products Circulation Promotion Group from promoting national products in Xuzhou, is enough to cause endless worry and doubt about the future of industry and commerce. Although the background to the occurrence of this phenomenon is complex, it further exposes an obvious fact that Chinese industry and commerce cannot have greater development in the face of intense dumping of foreign goods. As for the point of attention we should give to this matter, it is not about who is right and who is wrong between the National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association and the Sanshan Guildhall, but to explore the fundamental reasons why national industrial capital cannot develop.

Examining the origin of the so-called Zhuangke established by inland merchants from various provinces in Shanghai in the past, it was originally for purchasing foreign goods rather than selling national goods. As for local products (now known as national goods), most of them were traded locally, without the need for any Zhuangke. Later, because the sales of foreign goods became greater day by day, various so-called "national goods" made from foreign goods and improved local products emerged. Recently, general national goods have been manufactured effectively, and because of their lower prices, they can recover part of the inland market previously held by foreign goods. However, to facilitate the installation of machinery and the turnover of capital, most national goods factories are established in Shanghai, so the inland Zhuangke, originally established to purchase foreign goods, now also purchase national goods based on the principle of profitability.

The main cause of this dispute is not actually that the Zhuangke of the Sanshan Guildhall oppose the promotion of national goods, but that the Zhuangke's profits depend entirely on the benefit of reselling goods. Now that the Production and Sales Cooperation Association directly transports goods to Fujian to sell, it takes away the original benefits of the Zhuangke. Therefore, from the perspective of merchants seeking profit, it is only natural that the Zhuangke oppose it. But what we should pay attention to is that if the Shanghai industrial and commercial sectors do not quickly break this abnormal phenomenon during this time of intense competition from the dumping of foreign goods, then we will see that foreign goods can pass unhindered in the country, and if there is any obstruction, they will use cannons as weapons to break all obstacles, while national goods will not be able to be sold. If this continues, will the Chinese not truly be forever miserable people?

In practice, national goods factories should be widely established in various inland provinces, using local materials (raw materials, labor) for manufacturing, and promoting sales locally, which is a common phenomenon in other industrialized countries. Now, because our politics are not on track, most inland provinces suffer from natural disasters and man-made calamities every year, with bandits everywhere, rural economies are increasingly bankrupt, purchasing power is declining, and productivity is shrinking. As a result, no one dares to invest in establishing factories in the inland areas, and all new industries are concentrated in Shanghai. But what our industrial and commercial sectors should deeply realize is that this situation can only be maintained temporarily and is not a long-term plan. If we do not urgently seek remedies, then the miserable Chinese may not become slaves to a foreign country, but they will not be able to avoid becoming dead . So how should we rescue this dangerous situation? Should we just resign ourselves to fate and wait for death? These are all important matters that we should pay attention to.

The Chattering Yellow Birds 257

— Hua Tangdi

Autumn is deep, the west wind is blowing loudly. In the city, people, except for the penniless poor fellows, have all put on coats and camel hair. Foreign expatriate ladies may even have fox fur around their necks. Signs for "Yangcheng Lake Crabs" are everywhere in the market, with advertisements for one yuan each jumping before people's eyes: gourmets are naturally feasting, because they have "money" as a backing, but what about the penniless people? They can only swallow their cravings into their stomachs.

Following the "Crabs" that come on the market in this late autumn and early winter are the "Yellow Birds." When the rice grains are full in the fields in late autumn, the Yellow Birds become extremely active, regardless of how much blood and sweat the farmers have shed, regardless of whether they have to repay the landlords, and even regardless of whether they have to rely on this meager food to support their wives and daughters. All they do is "chatter" and eat the crops bare. The Yellow Birds also come in flocks, so eating them once is a great loss.

The farmers hate them. On the one hand, when it is time to harvest, they send people to guard the fields. On the other hand, they think of various ways to catch and kill these harmful creatures.

The farmers' capture of Yellow Birds has formed a kind of income in late autumn, but the hardship is enough to endure. The sun is still on the horizon, and the birds are singing hoarsely as they return to their nests. The Yellow Birds, of course, also want to run to their nests. Yellow Birds live in groups. Their nests are always deep in the reeds, so when dusk is approaching, the farmers are already waiting in secluded places. Waiting until they see the "clues," they are still not at ease. They slowly approach the reeds and go to the bank to observe. Only after careful observation and making sure that there are no errors do they go home to prepare. After preparing the necessary equipment for catching birds, they eat a full meal and then start dressing up. The so-called "dressing up" here is definitely not like the city women putting on powder and rouge before going out, nor is it like gentlemen tidying up their hats and clothes. It is just for the convenience of work that they open the buttons of their chest clothes, tie a thick board belt around their waist, take off their shoes and wear straw sandals, and bring the necessary equipment (the equipment is also very simple, but it is a long-handled silk net bucket and a dim kerosene lamp), and set off to the destination.

The water in the reed ponds in late autumn and early winter is probably a foot deep, not to mention the cold that penetrates to the bones. Sometimes there are also things like snakes lurking in it. But the farmers who are determined to make a living are not afraid of these. They quietly and silently step by step through the reeds, the water reaching their knees, but they do not care at all. They reach the place they have been watching, holding their breath, leaning on the reeds, and shining the dim kerosene lamp. As soon as they see their "target," they are overjoyed and hurriedly put the long-handled silk net bucket over it. Whether it is three or four birds in one net, they are all immediately strangled and placed on their exposed chest. If they are slightly careless, if even a single Yellow Bird makes a sound, all the others will escape. At this time, not only will they not catch anything themselves, but they will also implicate their companions, who will return empty-handed.

With skilled techniques and dexterity, a farmer can sell his catch for one or two thousand coins in one night. Although it is not enough for a bottle of champagne in a city lady's dance hall, it is a huge income for a farmer.

Basement 258

— Li Shulin

Because of the flood, we had to leave our hometown and flee. But where to flee to? Everywhere was flooded.

A foreign sampan came breaking through the waves, with a small red triangular flag of the ×× Church Refugee Relief Team fluttering at the stern and a guard holding a box cannon standing at the bow. We, a large group, originally wanted to rush forward (who wouldn't want to)? Around us was endless water, and a relief ship was coming), but looking at the cold little eyes of the box cannon, some people shouted a few times and then fell silent.

I can't remember how I was dragged onto the ship. When I woke up, I was already at the riverside of × port. The ship stopped, and we were all driven into freight cars, like bundles of goods. Li Axing, who had never ridden in a car before, vomited on someone in the shaking and rocking.

When we arrived at the ×× Church's ×× Association, we were placed in a basement room, packed full, lying down. After a while, a doctor in white came and said he was there for quarantine. I dragged the primary school student Yang Kai, wanting to go out and see the street scene, but was stopped at the gate. At this time, someone was asking and answering each other:

A: "Where are you going?"

B: "Upstairs to take a bath..."

Yang Kai and I both felt that we had taken baths in the water, but thinking about the stuffiness and heat on the ship and the musty smell in the basement, we both felt that it would be so nice to take a bath. We said in unison: "Let's go take a bath," and followed B into the elevator. But just as the elevator was about to close, a tall, thin person suddenly dragged us both out and asked where we were going.

"To take a bath," we said.

"Where do you live?" the man asked.

"In the basement."

"You think so highly of yourself," the man said with a sneer, "Do you know who can go upstairs? It costs three dollars a day!"

"Doesn't ×× preach equality and fraternity?" Yang Kai said bluntly.

"Humph!" the man widened his eyes, "There's nothing to say, you better know your place!"

"If we can't take a bath, why are you so fierce?" Yang Kai said angrily.

We couldn't take a bath, and we couldn't go out the door, so we had to go back to the basement again.

After a while, that tall guy came with a policeman, found me and Yang Kai, grabbed us by the collars, and shouted: "Get out! We don't want you living here!" We were silently pushed out the door, and in silence, we looked back at the face of that tall, Western-style building of compassionate benevolence.

We have no hope of entering Heaven.

Amateur Studies

Poor Scholar 259

— Duan Gu Xiang

Unfortunately, I was born into a poor family. When I was three or four years old, I heard my mother say: My father lost all of our ten acres of land because of his tobacco shop business! There was no other way, so he ran to Henan to become a soldier. Later, my older brother also followed him. This was during the "Marshal Wu" era. At that time, because I was too young, I couldn't carry a gun, so I missed the road of wearing "two-and-a-half-foot" uniforms and "eating big cakes."

There was no land at home to maintain our livelihood, so my mother took me to the city. I worked as a "maid" in a household, doing things like washing clothes, taking care of children, and buying vegetables, busy from morning to night without stopping! I, too, swept the guest rooms for them in the morning, brought wash water... In the evening, I waited for the mistress and master to come home, because they would go to the movies or the theater every day. As soon as the master saw me sitting down for a moment, he would stare at me with his frighteningly white eyes! Scolding me, cursing me: such a lazy little child! What good are you! I remember my head often being beaten by him until I was dizzy!

I messed around like this for three or four years. My desire for knowledge grew higher day by day. Whenever I saw the apple of their eyes—their little son—go to school or come back, I would feel an indescribable sadness and envy the children who could go to school; they were truly happy! Especially when I was twelve years old, I had to send the "little master" to school every day and then pick him up. Looking at the countless children in the school, the itchy feeling in my heart was really unbearable! I asked my mother several times, saying that I wanted to go to school and didn't want to suffer here anymore, but my mother didn't allow it and said sternly: "Where would the money come from! You'll starve to death outside!"

When I heard this, I became very angry. I always thought my mother's temper was too strange. As soon as the "little master" came back, the mistress would hug him and kiss him, calling him good boy, good boy, endlessly. I couldn't understand why my mother had such a cruel heart!

The normal school student who lived in the west wing happened to be on winter vacation at the time of my distress. We got along very well and often joked together. I often bought him things, so he especially liked me. As soon as we met, I would tell him about these problems, explaining that I was very willing to recognize a few characters and be able to write an account. But I was penniless, so what could I do?

He said: "It is true that studying requires money, but for someone his age, as long as he can work hard and study on his own after finishing his work, he can also make progress and acquire considerable knowledge. He also generously said: "When you have nothing to do in the evening, I can teach you to recognize two characters, as long as you are willing! Nothing is difficult in the world if you set your mind to it!"

He gave me a Thousand Character Classic and taught me to write and read every day. I would read the characters whenever I had nothing to do, and I would also practice writing on paper or on the ground. However, just when I was learning, either the master would have something to call me to do, or his classmates would come to find him to play. These things made me feel very annoyed, but I didn't lose heart because of this and continued to move forward.

Time flies like an arrow, and the winter vacation was over, so I stopped studying. But he was very concerned about me and told me to ask the master to allow me to go to the people's night school to study between 8:00 p.m. and 10:00 p.m. every night, because everyone had finished eating at this time, and the mistress and master would not return until 12:00 a.m., so there was nothing to do. If not, then simply break free and not bury my youthful body entirely in this place. I could do some small business to maintain my livelihood and go to the people's school at night to study.

My heart was moved by him. Surprisingly, I had enough courage to talk to the master that night. The result was a few cold laughs, and he said, "You eat, drink, and take money, and you still don't want to work!" He had a very contemptuous attitude. At that time, I was really furious and broke with the master. My mother was also fired. From then on, we began a new life.

I rented a thatched cottage outside the city, and my mother washed and mended clothes for the soldiers living in the nearby Guandi Temple every day. I did some small seasonal business, such as buying peanuts and melon seeds, and in the evening, I went to the people's night class to study. This continued for four years, and then I worked at the school for two more years.

Recalling the difficult life when my mother was occasionally sick, the freezing cold conditions, and the victory of the glorious lecture meeting, now that I can write letters and read vernacular books and newspapers, comparing these two situations, it is indeed very meaningful. Although I have suffered thousands of hardships in the past, I have certainly achieved considerable success. From this, it can be known that without resolute hard work, it is absolutely impossible to complete one's own and the public's cause and to obtain the joy of victory.
